Inheritance After Li'an and Ila': The Principle of Evasion (Farar) in Terminal Illness
Commentary on li'an and ila' cases from the matn, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on inheritance after li'an and ila' during terminal illness, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the li'an case.

Core Idea
In li'an and ila', inheritance turns on whether the separation is ultimately attributable to the husband's evasive action during illness.

When a terminally ill husband accuses his wife of adultery leading to li'an, or swears off marital relations (ila'), the question of inheritance arises. The Hanafi school has internal disagreement on the li'an case: did the husband's accusation constitute evasion, or did the wife's co-participation in the li'an break the connection? This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two situations: li'an after qadhf and ila'
The text discusses li'an (mutual cursing) after a husband accuses his wife of adultery, and ila' (vow of abstinence) that leads to divorce after four months.
2
State the default ruling for each
For li'an: there is ikhtilaf. Imam Abu Hanifah says she inherits; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she does not. For ila': she inherits if ila' was made while ill, but not if made while healthy.
The text notes that the matn restricts 'in his illness' to make the li'an case agreed upon, but then mentions the khilaf.
3
Trace the Hanafi proofs
Abu Hanifa: the husband's accusation forces the wife into li'an; the evasion is the accusation made in illness. Sahibayn: the wife's participation in li'an breaks attribution; no evasive act by husband in illness after accusation.
4
Apply the same principle to ila'
In ila', the separation is caused by the husband's inaction (failure to return within four months). If ila' begins in health, no evasion in illness; if begins in illness, evasion exists.
The commentary refutes an objection that the husband could have nullified ila' by returning (fi'), noting that this would cause him harm, so it is not considered.
5
Note the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view in the li'an case, as per al-Hidayah and the commentators.

[0] قوله : وكذا طالبة ... الخ ؛ فإنّها وإن رضيت بالطلاق لكنّها لم ترض بالإبانة، فإنّها طلبت الرجعي، فلما طلّقها ثلاثاً قصد الفرار عن الميراث، فاستحق الحرمان عن مقصوده. [1] قوله : ومبانة ؛ بصيغة المجهول من الإبانة، يعني طلق رجل زوجته ثلاثاً أو واحداً بائناً فاعتدت فارتكبت فعلاً تقعُ به الفرقة كتقبيل ابن الزوج ومطاوعته ، تكون وارثة ؛ لأنها وإن أتت بفعل يقعُ به الافتراق، لكن الافتراق لم يحصل به، بل بإبانته السابقة، فصار فعلها كعدمه، واحترز بقيد المبانة عن المطلقة طلاقاً رجعياً، فإنّها لو قبلت ابن الزوج في العدة لا ترث ؛ لأنّ البينونة جاءت من قبلها وبرضاها. [2] قوله : وهي في العدّة ؛ أي والحال أنها في العدّة فإن مضت العدة فلا يؤثر تقبيلها في شيء. [3]قوله : قذفها ؛ أي سبها وشتمها بالزنا، ولم يأتِ بأربعة شهداء يشهدون على ذلك. [4]قوله : في مرضه ؛ أي مرض موته ، قيَّد به مع أن عبارة المتن تشتمل ما إذا قذف في مرضه وما إذا قذف في صحته ولا عن في مرضه لتكون المسألة اتفاقية. فإنّ في الصورة الثانية خلافاً ذكره في «الهداية»، فعند محمد له لا ترث؛ لأنّ الطلاق إنّما وقع بلعانها ولم يوجد منه فعل يدلّ على الفرار، فإنّ القذف وقع منه قبله ، وعندهما : لا ترث ؛ لأنها مضطرة إلى اللعان بسبب قذفها، فكأنه وقعت البينونة منه في مرضه. [5] قوله : هذا ملحق ... الخ ؛ يعني يصير هذا كأنّ الزوج علّق الطلاق بفعل هي مضطرة في ارتكابه. [6] قوله : أو آلى ؛ ماض من الإيلاء، وسيجيء : تفسيره وحكمه في بابه. [7] قوله : مريضاً؛ أي حال كونه مريضاً بمرض الموت، وإنما قيد به لأنه لو الى امرأته وهو صحيح ومضت مدته في المرض ووقعت الفرقة لم ترث ؛ لأن البينونة مضافة في الإيلاء إلى فعل الزوج ، وقد وقع منه في الصحة ولم يوجد منه في مرضه شيء يصير به فاراً بخلاف ما إذا الى مريضاً ؛ لوجودِ سبب الفرقة منه في مرضه، فيصير فاراً به. فإن قلت : ينبغي أن يكون فاراً فيما إذا آلى في حال الصحة أيضاً ؛ لأنه كان يمكنه إبطال الإيلاء بالفيء، فإذا لم يبطله حتى مضت المدة ووقعت الفرقة في المرض صار كأنه أنشأ الإيلاء في المرض. قلت : إبطال الإيلاء لا يمكنه إلا بضرر يلزمه، فلا يعتبر به. كذا في «العناية» و«البناية».
And likewise a woman who sought a revocable divorce and was given three divorces, and a mubanah woman who kissed her husband’s son while she was in the waiting period, and one whom he accused of adultery in his illness then he performed li'an with her, or he performed ila' from her while being ill, likewise. [0] His statement: 'And likewise a woman who sought...' etc.; for she, although she consented to divorce, did not consent to final separation, for she sought revocable divorce. When he gave her three divorces, he intended to evade inheritance, so he deserved to be deprived of his objective. [1] His statement: 'And a mubanah woman' — in the passive form from ibanah, meaning a man divorced his wife three times or one irrevocable divorce, then she observed the waiting period and committed an act that causes separation, like kissing her husband’s son and being compliant with him: she is an inheritor; because although she performed an act that causes separation, the separation did not occur by it, but by his prior irrevocable divorce. So her act is considered as nothing. He restricted by the condition of mubanah to exclude the woman divorced revocably, for if she kissed her husband’s son during the waiting period, she does not inherit, because the irrevocable separation came from her and with her consent. [2] His statement: 'while she is in the waiting period' — meaning the situation is that she is in the waiting period; if the waiting period passes, her kissing has no effect. [3] His statement: 'he accused her' — meaning he insulted and slandered her with adultery, and did not produce four witnesses to testify to that. [4] His statement: 'in his illness' — meaning illness of death; he restricted with it even though the expression of the matn includes both cases: when he accused in his illness and when he accused in health but performed li'an in his illness, so that the issue would be agreed upon. For in the second case there is a difference mentioned in al-Hidayah: according to Muhammad, she does not inherit because the divorce occurred only by her li'an and there was no action from him indicating evasion, for the accusation occurred from him before it. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): she does not inherit because she is forced to li'an due to his accusation, so it is as if the separation occurred from him in his illness. [5] His statement: 'This is attached...' etc. — meaning this becomes as if the husband conditioned divorce upon an act she is forced to commit. [6] His statement: 'or he performed ila'' — past tense of ila'; its interpretation and ruling will come in its chapter. [7] His statement: 'while being ill' — meaning while being ill with fatal illness; he restricted with it because if he performed ila' from his wife while healthy and the period passed during illness and separation occurred, she does not inherit, because in ila' the separation is attributed to the husband’s action, and it occurred from him in health, and nothing occurred from him in his illness that would make him an evader, unlike the case when he performed ila' while ill, because the cause of separation occurred from him in his illness, so he becomes an evader by it. If you say: he should be considered an evader even when he performed ila' in health, because he could have nullified the ila' by returning (fi'), so if he did not nullify it until the period passed and separation occurred in illness, it becomes as if he initiated the ila' in illness. I say: nullifying the ila' is not possible for him except with harm that befalls him, so it is not considered. Thus it is in al-‘Inayah and al-Binayah.

Commentary
This passage discusses inheritance rulings for women separated from a terminally ill husband in specific scenarios. The central principle is that a woman inherits if the husband intended to deprive her of inheritance (farar), but not if she caused the final separation. The commentary expands on the matn, explaining each case. The first case: a woman who sought a revocable divorce (talāq raj‘ī) but her husband gave her three divorces (making it irrevocable). She inherits because she consented to revocable divorce, not to irrevocable separation. The husband’s act is deemed evasive. The second case: a woman already irrevocably divorced (mubānah) who kisses her husband’s son during her ‘iddah. She inherits because the irrevocable separation was already effected by the husband’s prior divorce; her subsequent act does not cause the separation. However, if she were in a revocable divorce, her kiss would create irrevocability and she would not inherit. The third case: a husband accuses his wife of adultery (qadhf) during his terminal illness, leading to li‘ān (mutual cursing) and consequent separation. Imām Abū Ḥanīfah holds that she inherits because the husband initiated the accusation. Imām Muḥammad and Imām Abū Yūsuf hold she does not inherit because the wife was forced into li‘ān and thus the separation is attributed to her. The Ḥanafī tarjīḥ (preferred view) is Abū Ḥanīfah’s. The fourth case: ilā’ (vow of abstinence) made while terminally ill. If the husband makes ilā’ while ill and the period expires causing irrevocable divorce, the wife inherits because the cause occurred in illness. If ilā’ was made while healthy and the period expires during illness, she does not inherit because the cause originated in health and no evasive action occurred in illness. The commentary refutes an objection that the husband could have nullified ilā’ by returning (fi’) by noting that nullification would harm him (e.g., violating his oath), so it is not a valid option.

Key Terms
لعان (li‘ān): Mutual cursing between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery without witnesses, resulting in permanent separation.
إيلاء (īlā’): A husband's vow to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for four months or more, leading to automatic divorce upon expiry if no compliance.
فرار (farār): The husband's act of depriving his wife of inheritance by divorcing her during terminal illness with the intention to exclude her.

In li'an and ila', the wife inherits only when the husband's evasive action (or its cause) occurred during his terminal illness, with the mufta bihi view for li'an being that the accusation in illness suffices.

Wife's Inheritance After Ila' or Li'an in Death Sickness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on li'an after death sickness divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's inheritance after divorce by ila' or li'an in the husband's death sickness and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding li'an.

Core Idea
In death sickness, a wife inherits despite divorce by ila'; for li'an, inheritance depends on who is deemed the cause of separation.

In Hanafi law, a husband who divorces his wife in terminal illness to deprive her of inheritance is considered to have 'fled' (farr), and the wife still inherits. But what about divorces triggered by the wife's own action, as in li'an? The classical Hanafi masters Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differed, and this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya dissects their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divorce mechanisms
The passage addresses ila' (a vow of abstinence leading to divorce after four months) and li'an (mutual imprecation due to false accusation of adultery). Understand the difference: in ila', the husband's action directly causes separation; in li'an, the wife's action triggers the divorce.
Ila' results in ba'in (irrevocable) divorce after the period; li'an results in permanent separation.
2
Understand the principle of firar (fleeing from inheritance)
If a husband divorces his wife in death sickness with the intention to exclude her from inheritance, he is a 'farr' (flee-er). The wife inherits despite the divorce to prevent his escape from her rightful share.
The key is whether his action in sickness indicates intent to flee.
3
Analyze the ruling for ila'
If the husband made ila' while sick and the period expired in his sickness, the separation occurred due to his action in sickness, making him a farr. Hence, the wife inherits.
Ila' made while healthy does not have the same effect because the cause of separation existed before sickness.
4
Examine the dispute on li'an
Abu Hanifa: wife inherits because the divorce occurred by her own li'an, not the husband's direct action in sickness. Sahibayn: wife does not inherit because she was compelled to li'an by his accusation, so separation is effectively his doing.
The dispute hinges on attribution of causation: is the husband's prior accusation part of the sickness?
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the wife inherits after li'an; under Sahibayn, she does not. Later Hanafi fatwa often favors Sahibayn, but the passage does not give a definitive tarjih.
Know both positions to understand the range of possible rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطلاق طلاق المريض أو آلي منها مريضاً كذلك فإن هذا ملحق بتعليق الطلاق بفعل لا بد للمرأة منه إذ لا بد لها من الخصومة لدفع العار عن نفسها. وقيل: أو آلى منها مريضاً كذلك أي حلف في مرض موته أن لا يقربها أربعة أشهر فلم يقربها حتى مضت المدة ووقعت البينونة ثم مات ترث. واختلف في اللعان: فعند أبي حنيفة ترث لأن الطلاق إنما وقع بلعانها ولم يوجد منه فعل يدل على الفرار فإن القذف وقع منه قبله. وعندهما: لا ترث لأنها مضطرة إلى اللعان بسبب قذفها فكأنه وقعت البينونة منه في مرضه. [١] قوله : هذا ملحق ... الخ ؛ يعني يصير هذا كأنّ الزوج علّق الطلاق بفعل هي مضطرة في ارتكابه. [٢] قوله : أو آلى ؛ ماض من الإيلاء، وسيجيء : تفسيره وحكمه في بابه. (٣) قوله : مريضاً؛ أي حال كونه مريضاً بمرض الموت، وإنما قيد به لأنه لو الى امرأته وهو صحيح ومضت مدته في المرض ووقعت الفرقة لم ترث ; لأن البينونة مضافة في الإيلاء إلى فعل الزوج ، وقد وقع منه في الصحة ولم يوجد منه في مرضه شيء يصير به فاراً بخلاف ما إذا الى مريضاً ; لوجودِ سبب الفرقة منه في مرضه، فيصير فاراً به. فإن قلت : ينبغي أن يكون فاراً فيما إذا آلى في حال الصحة أيضاً ; لأنه كان يمكنه إبطال الإيلاء بالفيء، فإذا لم يبطله حتى مضت المدة ووقعت الفرقة في المرض صار كأنه أنشأ الإيلاء في المرض. قلت : إبطال الإيلاء لا يمكنه إلا بضرر يلزمه، فلا يعتبر به.
Divorce of the sick person. Or he made ila' from her while sick likewise: this is attached to a conditional divorce by an act that the woman inevitably must do, since she must litigate to repel disgrace from herself. It is said: Or he made ila' from her while sick likewise, meaning he swore in his death sickness not to approach her for four months, and he did not approach her until the period passed and irrevocable separation occurred, then he died: she inherits. There is a difference of opinion regarding li'an: according to Abu Hanifa, she inherits because the divorce indeed occurred by her li'an and no act indicating his fleeing (firar) was found from him, for the accusation of adultery occurred before that. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): she does not inherit because she is compelled to li'an due to his accusation, so it is as if the separation occurred from him in his sickness. [1] He said: This is attached... etc., meaning this becomes as if the husband made divorce conditional upon an act she is compelled to commit. [2] He said: 'aw ala' is the past tense of ila', and its explanation and ruling will come in its section. (3) He said: 'mareedan' meaning in the state of being sick with a death sickness, and it is qualified because if he made ila' from his wife while healthy, and his period passed in sickness and separation occurred, she does not inherit because the separation in ila' is attributed to the husband's action, and it occurred while he was healthy and nothing appeared from him in his sickness that would make him a flee-er. But if he made ila' while sick, because the cause of separation occurred in his sickness, he becomes a flee-er. If you say: he should be considered a flee-er in the case of making ila' while healthy as well, because he could have annulled the ila' by returning (fi'), so if he did not annul it until the period passed and separation occurred in sickness, it is as if he initiated the ila' in sickness. The answer is: annulling ila' is not possible except with harm that befalls him, so it is not considered.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the ruling on a wife's inheritance when divorced by ila' or li'an during the husband's terminal illness. The author first states that if a man makes a vow of ila' (swearing not to approach his wife for four months) while on his deathbed, and the period expires causing an irrevocable divorce (ba'in), then the wife inherits from him if he dies. This is because the separation is attributed to the husband's action in his sickness, making him a 'far' (one who flees from inheritance rights). The author then discusses the case of li'an (mutual imprecation). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the wife inherits because the divorce occurred by her own action of li'an, not by the husband's volition, so he is not considered a flee-er. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that she does not inherit because she was compelled to initiate li'an due to the husband's false accusation, so the separation is effectively attributed to him in his sickness. The commentary also provides reasoning for why ila' in health does not make him a flee-er: because he could have annulled it by returning (fi'), but that would harm him, so it is not considered a voluntary escape.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A vow by a husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for four months or more.
اللعان (al-liʿān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses.
الفرار (al-firār): The act of a husband divorcing his wife in a terminal illness to deprive her of inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does a wife inherit from a husband who divorced her by ila' while on his deathbed?
A) Yes, because the separation occurred by his action in sickness.
B) No, because ila' is always initiated by the husband.
C) Yes, because all divorced wives inherit regardless of cause.
D) No, because ila' is not a valid divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wife inherits after ila' in death sickness; for li'an, the inheritance is disputed between Abu Hanifa (inherits) and Sahibayn (does not), with later practice favoring Sahibayn.

Cases Where a Wife Does Not Inherit After Divorce in Sickness
Listing cases where husband is not far or divorce is wife's initiative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific cases in which a wife does not inherit after divorce during the husband's illness and explain the legal principle behind each.

Core Idea
A wife inherits after divorce in sickness only if the husband's condition posed a predominant risk of death and he initiated the divorce.

In Hanafi inheritance law, a husband who divorces his wife while in a life-threatening state is considered a 'far' (one who flees from inheritance), and the wife may still inherit from him. However, not every divorce during illness triggers this ruling. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya enumerates specific situations where the wife does not inherit, either because the husband's condition is not life-threatening or because the divorce originates from the wife's own choice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle
The key concept is al-firar: only a husband in a state of predominant danger of death (makhuf al-halakah) is considered a flee-er. In other cases, the divorce is valid and cuts off inheritance.
The burden of proof lies on the wife to show the husband was in such a state.
2
Identify the first set of cases
List cases where the husband is not in predominant danger: doing household tasks outside complaining, having a fever, being besieged, standing in battle line (not yet fighting), imprisoned for retaliation or stoning (not yet executed), or in a plague-stricken area but not personally affected.
In all these, the risk of death is not immediate or predominant.
3
Identify the second set of cases
Cases where the divorce is by the wife's initiative: khul' (wife pays compensation), mukhayyara (wife chooses divorce when given option), or she requests triple talaq. In these, the separation is attributed to her volition, so the husband is not considered a flee-er.
Even if the husband is in death sickness, the wife does not inherit if she initiated the divorce.
4
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a new factual scenario, determine whether the husband's condition was life-threatening and whether the divorce was his act or hers. This determines the wife's inheritance right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قام بها خارج البيت مشتكياً، أو حمّ، ومن هو محصور، أو في صف القتال، أو حبس بقصاص، أو رجم صحيح إن طلقت، وهو كذلك لا ترث. وكذا المختلعة، ومخيّرة اختارت نفسها، ومَن طُلقت ثلاثاً بأمرها. [١]- (ومن قام بها خارج البيت مشتكياً ، أو حمّ، ومَن هو محصور، أو في صف القتال ، أو حبس بقصاص ، أو رجم صحيح إن طلقت) : أي طلاقاً بائناً ، (وهو كذلك لا ترث. وكذا المختلعة، ومخيّرة اختارت نفسها (٢) ، ومَن طُلقت ثلاثاً بأمرها (1) قوله : ومن قام ... الخ ؛ شروع في بيان الأصحاء الذين لا يكونون فارين بطلاقهم ولا ترث زوجتهم. فمنهم من قام بمصالح البيت خارجه مشتكياً من ألم ، فإنّه لا يغلب عليه خوف الهلاك، بخلاف من عجز عن ذلك. ومنهم من حُم وهو مجهول ; - أي صار محموماً - فإن مجرد الحمى لا يخافُ منه الهلاك غالباً. وكذا من هو محصور ; أي محبوس بحصن ظلماً أو إنصافاً. وكذا من هو في صف القتال وإن كان قاصداً مهيّئاً له ولم يخرج بعد للمبارزة ، بخلاف ما إذا خرج مبارزاً واختلط بخصمه. وكذا من حبس في محبس بسبب وجوب قصاص عليه أو رجم ما لم يقدّم للقتل. وكذا من هو في بلدة فشا فيها الطاعون ونحوه، صرح به الحافظ ابن العسقلاني في رسالتِهِ في بحث الطاعون المسماة بـ«بذل الماعون»، وصاحب «البحر» في «الأشباه والنظائر» وغيرهما، وبالجملة : فمَن لم يخف فيه الهلاك غالباً يعد صحيحاً، فلا يكون فاراً بطلاقه في تلك الحالة. [٢] قوله : وكذا ; أي لا ترث الزوجة التي اختلعت من زوجها في مرض موته، والمخيرة بخيار البلوغ أو خيار العتق اختارت نفسها في مرض موته، أو التي قال لها زوجها : اختاري فاختارت نفسها في مرض موته ، فإنّ الفرقة في هذه الصورة جاءت من قبلها.
And whoever performs household tasks outside the house complaining, or has a fever, and whoever is besieged, or in the battle line, or imprisoned for retaliation, or for stoning while healthy, if she is divorced (and he is thus), she does not inherit. And likewise the one divorced by khul', and the wife given a choice who chooses herself, and the one divorced three times at her request. [1] (And whoever performs household tasks outside the house complaining, or has a fever, and whoever is besieged, or in the battle line, or imprisoned for retaliation, or for stoning while healthy, if she is divorced) meaning an irrevocable divorce, (and he is thus, she does not inherit. And likewise the one divorced by khul', and the wife given a choice who chooses herself, and the one divorced three times at her request.) (1) He said: 'And whoever performs...' etc.; beginning to explain healthy persons who are not considered flee-ers by their divorce and their wife does not inherit. Among them is one who performs household tasks outside the house complaining of pain, for the fear of death does not overcome him, unlike one who is incapable of that. And among them is one who has a fever while the type is unknown - i.e., he became feverish - for mere fever does not usually lead to fear of death. And likewise whoever is besieged, i.e., imprisoned in a fortress unjustly or justly. And likewise whoever is in the battle line, even if he is intending and prepared for it and has not yet gone out for duel, unlike if he went out as a duelist and mingled with his opponent. And likewise whoever is imprisoned in a prison due to an obligation of retaliation against him or stoning, as long as he has not been brought forth for execution. And likewise whoever is in a town where plague or the like has spread, as stated by al-Hafiz Ibn al-Sayqalani in his treatise on plague called 'Bazl al-Ma'un', and the author of 'al-Bahr' in 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir' and others. In summary, whoever does not have a predominant fear of death is considered healthy, so he is not a flee-er by his divorce in that state. [2] He said: 'Likewise' meaning the wife who made khul' from her husband in his death sickness does not inherit, and the wife given a choice (mukhayyara) by reaching puberty or manumission who chooses herself in his death sickness, or the one whose husband said to her 'choose' and she chose herself in his death sickness, for the separation in this scenario came from her side.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya enumerates cases where a husband divorces his wife while sick but is not considered a 'far' (flee-er), so the wife does not inherit from him if he dies. The principle is that only if the husband's condition poses a predominant risk of death does the divorce count as fleeing. The listed cases are: (1) a husband who manages household affairs outside while complaining of pain (not bedridden), (2) one with a fever (unknown type, not necessarily fatal), (3) one besieged in a fortress, (4) one in the battle line but not yet engaged in duel, (5) one imprisoned for retaliation or stoning but not yet executed, (6) one in a town with plague but not necessarily affected. In all these, the risk of death is not predominant, so the husband is considered healthy in terms of inheritance law. Additionally, the passage notes that if the divorce occurs at the wife's request (khul', choice, or triple divorce at her behest), she does not inherit because the separation is attributed to her volition, not to the husband's attempt to deprive her of inheritance.

Key Terms
المختلعة (al-mukhtaliʿa): A wife who obtains a divorce through khul' (redemption) by paying compensation to the husband.
المخيرة (al-mukhayyara): A wife given the choice of remaining married or divorcing, often in cases of option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) or option after manumission.
الفرار (al-firār): The concept of a husband divorcing his wife to exclude her from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following scenarios does the wife NOT inherit if she is divorced in her husband's terminal illness?
A) The husband makes ila' while on his deathbed.
B) The husband divorces her while he is healthy but later falls ill and dies.
C) The wife initiates khul' in the husband's death sickness.
D) The husband divorces her by li'an in his death sickness according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wife's inheritance after divorce during sickness depends on two factors: the husband's state of predominant danger and who initiated the divorce.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Situations Where a Husband is Not Considered Fleeing
Explains healthy situations where husband is not farr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific situations where a husband's divorce during illness does not prevent inheritance and apply the general principle that only imminent fear of death triggers farr.

Core Idea
A husband is not fleeing inheritance if his condition does not generally inspire fear of death.

This lesson from the commentary on al-Wiqayah enumerates cases where a husband's divorce does not make him a 'farr' (fleeing from inheritance). The rule is that if the husband is not in imminent danger of death, his divorce is valid and the wife does not inherit. The text lists several scenarios: performing household tasks outside while complaining, fever, siege, being in the battle line without dueling, imprisonment for retaliation or stoning, and being in a plague-stricken town. The common thread is that death is not generally feared.

Guided Path
1
List the enumerated cases
Identify each situation mentioned: tasks outside with complaint, fever, besieged, in battle line, imprisoned for retaliation/stoning, in plague town. Write them down.
Also note the exception: going out to duel makes the husband potentially fleeing.
2
Find the common element
Determine what all these cases share. The text states: 'whoever does not generally fear destruction therein is considered healthy.' The key is the absence of ghālibat al-halak.
3
Apply the general principle
State the principle: If the husband's condition does not lead to a general fear of death, he is considered healthy for inheritance purposes, and his divorce does not make him a fleer.
This principle distinguishes farr from non-farr cases.
4
Distinguish from farr cases
Contrast with a husband who is bedridden or has a terminal illness where death is likely. In those cases, if he divorces without wife's request, she inherits.
The line is drawn at ghālibat al-halak.
5
Derive the ruling
In each enumerated scenario, the wife does not inherit. The divorce is valid, and the husband is not considered to have acted to deprive her.

[٢] قوله : وكذا ؛ أي لا ترث الزوجة التي اختلعت من زوجها في مرض موته ، والمخيرة بخيار البلوغ أو خيار العتق اختارت نفسها في مرض موته، أو التي قال لها زوجها : اختاري فاختارت نفسها في مرض موته ، فإنّ الفرقة في هذه الصورة جاءت بفعلها ورضاها، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك لا يصير الزوج فيه فاراً. [ ١ ] قوله : ثمّ صح ؛ هذا قيد لقوله : لا بأمرها ، فإنّه إذا طلبت الثلاث ورضيت، ففعل ما طلبته لا ترث سواءً صح من مرضه ذلك أو لم يصح؛ لأنه طلقها برضاها ، فلم يعد فاراً، وأما إذا طلقها ثلاثاً لا برضاها فإن مات في ذلك المرض ترث ؛ لأنه فارّ بالطلاق وإن صح من ذلك المرض ثم مات بسبب آخر لا ترث لفناء حكم الفرار، بتخلل الصحة. [٢] قوله : ولو تصادق ؛ يعني توافق الزوجة والزوج المريض بمرض الموت على وقوع ثلاث في الصحة، وعلى تمام العدة، بأن قال الزوج في مرض موته : كنت طلقتك ثلاثا في صحتي، وانقضت عدتك فصدقته، أو قالت الزوجة : كنت طلقتني ثلاثاً حال صحتك، وانقضت عدتي فصدقها. [۳] قوله : على ثلاث ؛ وكذا لو توافقا على إيقاع واحد أو اثنين، ومضي العدة. [٤]قوله : ومضي العدة ؛ عطف على قوله : «ثلاث» ؛ أي وقع التصادق على كل من الأمرين : وقوع الثلاث حال الصحة وانقضاء العدة. وقيد به ليظهر خلافُ الصاحبين فيه ، فإنّه لو لم يتصادقا على مضي العدة فلها الأقل اتفاقاً ، قال ابن الهمام في فتح القدير ) : هاتان مسألتان ما إذا تصادقا في مرض موتِهِ على طلاقها وانقضاء عدتها قبل المرض، وما إذا أنشأ الطلاق ثلاثاً في مرضها بسؤالها ، ثمّ أقر لها بمال أو أوصى لها بوصية.
And whoever performs (household tasks) outside the house complaining (of pain), or is feverish, and whoever is besieged, or in the battle line, or imprisoned for retaliation, or for valid stoning, if she is divorced: meaning an irrevocable divorce, and he is in that state, she does not inherit. Likewise the woman who obtains khul', and the woman given a choice who chose herself, and the woman who is divorced three times by her command. His saying: 'And whoever performs...' is a beginning to explain the healthy who are not considered fleeing by their divorce and whose wife does not inherit. Among them is the one who performs the household tasks outside the house complaining of pain, for fear of destruction does not overcome him, unlike the one who is unable to do that. Among them is the one who is feverish, which is unknown; that is, became feverish, for mere fever is not generally feared to cause destruction. Likewise the one who is besieged; that is, imprisoned in a fort unjustly or justly. Likewise the one who is in the battle line even if he intends and is prepared for it and has not yet gone out to duel; unlike when he goes out to duel and mixes with his opponent. Likewise the one who is imprisoned in a prison due to necessity of retaliation or stoning as long as he has not been brought forward for execution. Likewise the one who is in a town where plague and the like have spread; the Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani stated it in his treatise on research on plague named 'Bazl al-Ma'un', and the author of 'al-Bahr' in 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir' and others. In summary: whoever does not generally fear destruction therein is considered healthy, so he is not fleeing by his divorce in that state. His saying: 'Likewise'; that is, the wife who obtained khul' from her husband in his terminal illness does not inherit, and the woman given a choice upon reaching puberty or upon being freed who chose herself in his terminal illness, or the one to whom her husband said 'Choose!' and she chose herself in his terminal illness; for the separation in this case came by her action and consent, and whatever is like that does not make the husband a flee-er. His saying: 'Then he recovered'; this is a condition for his saying 'not by her command', because if she requested the three divorces and consented, and he did what she requested, she does not inherit whether he recovered from that illness or not; because he divorced her with her consent, so he is not considered a flee-er. But if he divorced her three times without her consent, then if he dies in that illness she inherits because he is fleeing by divorce; and if he recovers from that illness and then dies from another cause, she does not inherit because the effect of fleeing has ended, due to the interposition of health. His saying: 'And if they mutually attest'; meaning the wife and the husband suffering from terminal illness agree upon the occurrence of three (divorces) in health, and upon the completion of the 'iddah: by the husband saying in his terminal illness: 'I divorced you three times in my health, and your 'iddah ended', and she confirms him; or the wife says: 'You divorced me three times in your health, and my 'iddah ended', and he confirms her. His saying: 'upon three'; likewise if they agree upon one or two, and the passing of the 'iddah. His saying: 'and the passing of the 'iddah'; it is a conjunction to his saying 'three'; that is, the mutual attestation occurred upon both matters: the occurrence of the three in health and the expiry of the 'iddah. And it was conditioned to show the disagreement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) about it, because if they did not mutually attest to the passing of the 'iddah, then she gets the minimum (of the period) by agreement. Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: 'These are two issues: when they mutually attest in his terminal illness to her divorce and the expiry of her 'iddah before the illness; and when he initiated the three divorces in her illness at her request, then he acknowledged a debt for her or bequeathed to her a legacy.'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on al-Wiqayah explains the rule that a wife inherits from her husband only if he divorced her while fleeing from inheritance (farr). The commentator details cases where the husband is not considered fleeing because he is not in imminent danger of death. These include: a husband who performs household tasks outside while complaining of pain (not bedridden), one with a fever (since fever alone is not usually fatal), one besieged in a fort (whether justly or unjustly), one in the battle line (but not yet engaged in dueling), one imprisoned for retaliation or stoning (but not yet brought for execution), and one in a plague-stricken town (as per Ibn Hajar and others). The underlying principle is that if the husband does not generally fear death (ghalabat al-halak), he is considered healthy and his divorce does not make him a fleer. The passage then addresses cases where the wife initiated the separation: khul', option of puberty, option after emancipation, or if she requested and consented to a triple divorce. In these, the wife does not inherit because the separation was by her choice. However, if the husband divorced her three times without her command, and dies in that illness, she inherits because he is fleeing; if he recovers and dies later, she does not inherit because the taint of fleeing is removed by recovery. Finally, the passage discusses the scenario where both spouses mutually attest that the triple divorce occurred during health and the 'iddah has passed. In that case, the wife does not inherit because the divorce was in health. There is a disagreement with the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the effect of the 'iddah; the commentator notes that if they did not attest to the passing of the 'iddah, she gets the minimum 'iddah by agreement, and the Sahibayn differed on other points.

Key Terms
فارّ (farr): A husband who divorces his wife while terminally ill with the intent to deprive her of inheritance; legally, he is considered fleeing from inheritance.
محصور (mahsur): One who is besieged or confined in a fort, whether justly or unjustly, as an example of a situation where death is not imminently feared.
غالب الهلاك (ghālibat al-halak): General fear of destruction or death; the threshold used to determine whether a husband is considered fleeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following husbands IS considered fleeing (farr) and thus his wife inherits if he dies in that condition?
A) A husband performing household tasks outside while complaining of a headache.
B) A husband with a mild fever.
C) A husband who has gone out to duel in battle.
D) A husband imprisoned for a debt and in good health.

Key Takeaway
A husband is not fleeing from inheritance unless his condition at the time of divorce creates a general fear of death (ghālibat al-halak).

Wife-Initiated Separation: Khul', Choice, and Request
Explains wife-initiated separations and inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three situations where a wife does not inherit from her husband who divorced her during terminal illness because she initiated the separation.

Core Idea
A wife who causes the separation does not inherit, even in terminal illness.

This section of the commentary addresses cases where the wife herself sought the divorce or accepted a separation. These include khul' (divorce with compensation), exercising the option of puberty or emancipation, or requesting a triple divorce. In these cases, the husband is not considered fleeing, so the wife does not inherit. The common principle is that the separation came about by the wife's action or consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The text lists: (1) wife obtains khul', (2) wife chooses herself when given an option (puberty/emancipation), (3) wife is divorced three times at her own command. List them.
All three occur during the husband's terminal illness.
2
Determine the common element
In each case, the wife actively causes or consents to the separation. The husband does not act unilaterally.
The text says: 'الفرقة في هذه الصورة جاءت بفعلها ورضاها'.
3
Derive the ruling
Because the wife initiated, the husband is not fleeing (farr), and she does not inherit. The divorce is valid and the inheritance right is negated.

[٢] قوله : ولو تصادق ؛ يعني توافق الزوجة والزوج المريض بمرض الموت على وقوع ثلاث في الصحة، وعلى تمام العدة، بأن قال الزوج في مرض موته : كنت طلقتك ثلاثا في صحتي، وانقضت عدتك فصدقته، أو قالت الزوجة : كنت طلقتني ثلاثاً حال صحتك، وانقضت عدتي فصدقها. [۳] قوله : على ثلاث ؛ وكذا لو توافقا على إيقاع واحد أو اثنين، ومضي العدة. [٤]قوله : ومضي العدة ؛ عطف على قوله : «ثلاث» ؛ أي وقع التصادق على كل من الأمرين : وقوع الثلاث حال الصحة وانقضاء العدة. وقيد به ليظهر خلافُ الصاحبين فيه ، فإنّه لو لم يتصادقا على مضي العدة فلها الأقل اتفاقاً ، قال ابن الهمام في فتح القدير ) : هاتان مسألتان ما إذا تصادقا في مرض موتِهِ على طلاقها وانقضاء عدتها قبل المرض، وما إذا أنشأ الطلاق ثلاثاً في مرضها بسؤالها ، ثمّ أقر لها بمال أو أوصى لها بوصية.
And whoever performs (household tasks) outside the house complaining (of pain), or is feverish, and whoever is besieged, or in the battle line, or imprisoned for retaliation, or for valid stoning, if she is divorced: meaning an irrevocable divorce, and he is in that state, she does not inherit. Likewise the woman who obtains khul', and the woman given a choice who chose herself, and the woman who is divorced three times by her command. His saying: 'And whoever performs...' is a beginning to explain the healthy who are not considered fleeing by their divorce and whose wife does not inherit. Among them is the one who performs the household tasks outside the house complaining of pain, for fear of destruction does not overcome him, unlike the one who is unable to do that. Among them is the one who is feverish, which is unknown; that is, became feverish, for mere fever is not generally feared to cause destruction. Likewise the one who is besieged; that is, imprisoned in a fort unjustly or justly. Likewise the one who is in the battle line even if he intends and is prepared for it and has not yet gone out to duel; unlike when he goes out to duel and mixes with his opponent. Likewise the one who is imprisoned in a prison due to necessity of retaliation or stoning as long as he has not been brought forward for execution. Likewise the one who is in a town where plague and the like have spread; the Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani stated it in his treatise on research on plague named 'Bazl al-Ma'un', and the author of 'al-Bahr' in 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir' and others. In summary: whoever does not generally fear destruction therein is considered healthy, so he is not fleeing by his divorce in that state. His saying: 'Likewise'; that is, the wife who obtained khul' from her husband in his terminal illness does not inherit, and the woman given a choice upon reaching puberty or upon being freed who chose herself in his terminal illness, or the one to whom her husband said 'Choose!' and she chose herself in his terminal illness; for the separation in this case came by her action and consent, and whatever is like that does not make the husband a flee-er. His saying: 'Then he recovered'; this is a condition for his saying 'not by her command', because if she requested the three divorces and consented, and he did what she requested, she does not inherit whether he recovered from that illness or not; because he divorced her with her consent, so he is not considered a flee-er. But if he divorced her three times without her consent, then if he dies in that illness she inherits because he is fleeing by divorce; and if he recovers from that illness and then dies from another cause, she does not inherit because the effect of fleeing has ended, due to the interposition of health. His saying: 'And if they mutually attest'; meaning the wife and the husband suffering from terminal illness agree upon the occurrence of three (divorces) in health, and upon the completion of the 'iddah: by the husband saying in his terminal illness: 'I divorced you three times in my health, and your 'iddah ended', and she confirms him; or the wife says: 'You divorced me three times in your health, and my 'iddah ended', and he confirms her. His saying: 'upon three'; likewise if they agree upon one or two, and the passing of the 'iddah. His saying: 'and the passing of the 'iddah'; it is a conjunction to his saying 'three'; that is, the mutual attestation occurred upon both matters: the occurrence of the three in health and the expiry of the 'iddah. And it was conditioned to show the disagreement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) about it, because if they did not mutually attest to the passing of the 'iddah, then she gets the minimum (of the period) by agreement. Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: 'These are two issues: when they mutually attest in his terminal illness to her divorce and the expiry of her 'iddah before the illness; and when he initiated the three divorces in her illness at her request, then he acknowledged a debt for her or bequeathed to her a legacy.'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on al-Wiqayah explains the rule that a wife inherits from her husband only if he divorced her while fleeing from inheritance (farr). The commentator details cases where the husband is not considered fleeing because he is not in imminent danger of death. These include: a husband who performs household tasks outside while complaining of pain (not bedridden), one with a fever (since fever alone is not usually fatal), one besieged in a fort (whether justly or unjustly), one in the battle line (but not yet engaged in dueling), one imprisoned for retaliation or stoning (but not yet brought for execution), and one in a plague-stricken town (as per Ibn Hajar and others). The underlying principle is that if the husband does not generally fear death (ghalabat al-halak), he is considered healthy and his divorce does not make him a fleer. The passage then addresses cases where the wife initiated the separation: khul', option of puberty, option after emancipation, or if she requested and consented to a triple divorce. In these, the wife does not inherit because the separation was by her choice. However, if the husband divorced her three times without her command, and dies in that illness, she inherits because he is fleeing; if he recovers and dies later, she does not inherit because the taint of fleeing is removed by recovery. Finally, the passage discusses the scenario where both spouses mutually attest that the triple divorce occurred during health and the 'iddah has passed. In that case, the wife does not inherit because the divorce was in health. There is a disagreement with the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the effect of the 'iddah; the commentator notes that if they did not attest to the passing of the 'iddah, she gets the minimum 'iddah by agreement, and the Sahibayn differed on other points.

Key Terms
مختلعة (mukhtali'ah): A wife who obtains khul' (divorce by compensation) from her husband during his terminal illness; she does not inherit because the separation was by her choice.
مخيّرة (mukhayyarah): A wife who is given a choice (e.g., at puberty or after emancipation) and selects herself (i.e., divorce); she does not inherit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following wives does NOT inherit from her terminally ill husband who divorces her?
A) A wife who did not consent and was divorced unilaterally.
B) A wife who was given an option at puberty and chose to stay.
C) A wife who paid compensation for khul'.
D) A wife whose husband divorced her without her knowledge.

Key Takeaway
A wife who initiates or consents to a divorce from a terminally ill husband does not inherit, because the separation is by her choice.

Recovery and Mutual Attestation: Fleeing Status and the Sahibayn Disagreement
Explains recovery and mutual attestation with Sahibayn ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the effect of the husband's recovery on the wife's inheritance and analyze the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding mutual attestation of divorce and 'iddah.

Core Idea
If the husband recovers, the wife's inheritance right is extinguished; mutual attestation of a prior divorce in health negates inheritance, but the Sahibayn differ on the 'iddah condition.

This lesson covers two important nuances within the farr concept. First, if the husband divorces without the wife's request and then recovers from his terminal illness, the wife does not inherit if he dies later. Second, if both spouses mutually attest that a triple divorce occurred in health and the 'iddah expired, she does not inherit. However, a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn) arises if the attestation of the 'iddah expiry is missing.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the recovery scenario
The text distinguishes: if husband divorces three times without wife's request, then recovers, the wife does not inherit. The 'fleeing' taint is removed by health.
If he dies in that illness, she inherits. So the recovery changes the outcome.
2
Understand mutual attestation
Both spouses agree in the husband's terminal illness that he divorced her in health and her 'iddah has expired. This confirms the divorce occurred before illness, so no fleeing.
The attestation is accepted as true.
3
Identify the Sahibayn disagreement
Abu Hanifa requires attesting to both the divorce and the 'iddah expiry. If only the divorce is attested but not 'iddah, she does not inherit? Actually, the text says: if they do not attest to 'iddah expiry, she gets the minimum 'iddah by agreement. The Sahibayn differ on the effect.
Ibn al-Humam mentions two issues.
4
Apply the ruling
In the case of full attestation, wife does not inherit. In incomplete attestation (only divorce), there is ikhtilaf; but the mainstream Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) holds she does not inherit.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

(ومن قام بها خارج البيت مشتكياً ، أو حمّ، ومَن هو محصور، أو في صف القتال ، أو حبس بقصاص ، أو رجم صحيح إن طلقت) : أي طلاقاً بائناً ، (وهو كذلك لا ترث. وكذا المختلعة، ومخيّرة اختارت نفسها ، ومَن طُلقت ثلاثاً بأمرها (1) قوله : ومن قام ... الخ ؛ شروع في بيان الأصحاء الذين لا يكونون فارين بطلاقهم ولا ترث زوجتهم. فمنهم من قام بمصالح البيت خارجه مشتكياً من ألم ، فإنّه لا يغلب عليه خوف الهلاك، بخلاف من عجز عن ذلك. ومنهم من حُم وهو مجهول ؛ - أي صار محموماً - فإن مجرد الحمى لا يخافُ منه الهلاك غالباً. وكذا من هو محصور ؛ أي محبوس بحصن ظلماً أو إنصافاً. وكذا من هو في صف القتال وإن كان قاصداً مهيّئاً له ولم يخرج بعد للمبارزة ، ! بخلاف ما إذا خرج مبارزاً واختلط بخصمه. وكذا من حبس في محبس بسبب وجوب قصاص عليه أو رجم ما لم يقدّم للقتل. وكذا من هو في بلدة فشا فيها الطاعون ونحوه، صرح به الحافظ ابن العسقلاني في رسالتِهِ في بحث الطاعون المسماة بـ«بذل الماعون»، وصاحب «البحر» في «الأشباه والنظائر» وغيرهما، وبالجملة : فمَن لم يخف فيه الهلاك غالباً يعد صحيحاً، فلا يكون فاراً بطلاقه في تلك الحالة. [ ١ ] قوله : ثمّ صح ؛ هذا قيد لقوله : لا بأمرها ، فإنّه إذا طلبت الثلاث ورضيت، ففعل ما طلبته لا ترث سواءً صح من مرضه ذلك أو لم يصح؛ لأنه طلقها برضاها ، فلم يعد فاراً، وأما إذا طلقها ثلاثاً لا برضاها فإن مات في ذلك المرض ترث ؛ لأنه فارّ بالطلاق وإن صح من ذلك المرض ثم مات بسبب آخر لا ترث لفناء حكم الفرار، بتخلل الصحة. الصاحبان (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Divorce by a Sick Person and Inheritance Rights
Commentarial expansion on inheritance from sick divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance when a sick person divorces his wife with or without her consent, and identify the condition that nullifies the inheritance right.

Core Idea
If a sick man divorces his wife without her consent, she inherits if he dies in that illness; recovery before death nullifies her inheritance.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expands on the ruling regarding inheritance after a divorce pronounced during a fatal illness (marad al-mawt). The key distinction is whether the wife requested the divorce or not, and whether the husband recovers. The school protects the wife's right to inheritance while preventing abuse of the divorce mechanism to deprive her of her share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: divorce by a sick person (ṭalāq al-marīḍ). The ruling concerns whether the wife inherits from the husband after such a divorce.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Separate the case where the wife requested the divorce (with her consent) from the case where she did not (without her consent). In the first, she does not inherit regardless of recovery. In the second, inheritance depends on recovery.
3
Apply the condition of recovery
If the husband divorces without her consent and then recovers from the illness, the taint of firar (fleeing from inheritance) is removed. If he later dies from another cause, she does not inherit. Only if he dies in that same illness does she inherit.
Recovery means complete recovery from the fatal illness that prompted the divorce.
4
Understand the basis: firar
The concept of firar (fugitive) is central: if the husband divorces to deprive his wife of inheritance, the law treats it as an attempted evasion. That evasion is only relevant if he dies in that illness. Recovery shows he was not actually fleeing, so the normal inheritance rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق طلاق المريض
أو لا بأمرها، ثم صح.
قوله: أو لا بأمرها ثم صح: أي صح من مرضه، ثم مات لا ترث.
[١] قوله: ثم صح؛ هذا قيد لقوله: لا بأمرها، فإنه إذا طلبت الثلاث ورضيت ففعل ما طلبت لا ترث سواء صح من مرضه ذلك أو لم يصح؛ لأنه طلقها برضاها فلم يعد فاراً، وأما إذا طلقها ثلاثاً لا برضاها فإن مات في ذلك المرض ترث؛ لأنه فار بالطلاق، وإن صح من ذلك المرض ثم مات بسبب آخر لا ترث لفناء حكم الفرار بتخلل الصحة.
Book of Divorce: Divorce of the Sick Person. Or not by her command, then he recovered. His saying: 'or not by her command then he recovered' means: he recovered from his illness, then died, she does not inherit. [1] His saying 'then he recovered' is a condition for his saying 'not by her command'. For if she requested the three and consented, and he did what she requested, she does not inherit, whether he recovered from that illness or not, because he divorced her with her consent, so he is not considered a fugitive (farr). But if he divorced her three times without her consent, then if he dies in that illness, she inherits because he is a fugitive by divorce; and if he recovers from that illness then dies due to another cause, she does not inherit due to the nullification of the ruling of fugitive status by the interposition of recovery.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqaya regarding the divorce of a sick person. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If the wife requested the divorce and consented, then even if the husband dies in his illness after divorcing her, she does not inherit because the divorce was with her consent, so it is not considered an attempt to deprive her of inheritance (firar). (2) If the divorce was without her request, then the husband is considered to be fleeing from her inheritance right, so if he dies in that illness, she inherits. However, if he recovers from that illness and later dies from another cause, the taint of firar is removed, and she does not inherit. The key condition is that the divorce must be in his fatal illness (marad al-mawt). The ruling is based on the principle of protecting the wife's right to inheritance within the window of the illness.

Key Terms
فارّ (fārr): One who flees from the obligation of inheritance by divorcing his wife in fatal illness without her consent.
طلاق المريض (ṭalāq al-marīḍ): Divorce pronounced by a person in a fatal illness (marad al-mawt), which may be subject to special inheritance rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick man divorces his wife three times without her consent, then recovers and later dies of another cause, does she inherit?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, because recovery nullifies the firar status.
C) Yes, because the divorce was without consent.
D) No, because she requested it.

Key Takeaway
A wife inherits from a sick husband's divorce only if he divorced her without her consent and died in that illness; recovery before death removes her inheritance right.

Mutual Confirmation of Divorce and Acknowledgment: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Analyses intra-Hanafi dispute on acknowledgment/bequest after mutual confirmation of divorce in health

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, Zufar) on the limitation of a terminally ill husband's iqrār or wasiyya to his divorced wife after mutual confirmation of divorce in health, and explain the reasoning based on tuhma.

Core Idea
Suspicion persists even after divorce and idda, limiting the wife's entitlement under Abu Hanifa.

When a terminally ill husband acknowledges a debt or makes a bequest to his divorced wife after both confirm that the divorce occurred in health and the waiting period ended, the Hanafi school scrutinizes the transaction for potential collusion. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the wife receives the full amount or only the lesser of her hypothetical inheritance share and the bequest. The key issue is whether the suspicion (tuhma) is tied to the ongoing idda or to the prior marital bond itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two spouses mutually confirm (tasāduq) during the husband's fatal illness that he divorced her three times while healthy and that her idda ended before the illness. Following this, the husband acknowledges a debt or makes a bequest to her.
The mutual confirmation establishes that she is not an heir.
2
List the three positions
Abu Hanifa: She takes the lesser of the inheritance share (if she were an heir) and the bequest/acknowledgment. Zufar: She takes the full bequest/acknowledgment. Sahibayn: In the case where the idda ended before illness, she takes the full amount (like Zufar); in the case where divorce was at her request during illness, she takes the lesser (like Abu Hanifa).
The two cases differ based on when the divorce occurred relative to illness and idda.
3
Understand the concept of tuhma (suspicion)
Tuhma is the suspicion that the couple colluded to give the wife more than her inheritance share, to the detriment of other heirs. The dispute centers on when this suspicion arises.
Zufar denies tuhma once idda ends. Sahibayn tie it to the existence of idda. Abu Hanifa argues it arises from the prior marriage bond itself.
4
Analyze the reasoning of each position
Zufar: The mutual confirmation nullifies the inheritance impediment, so no suspicion. Sahibayn: In the first case (idda ended before illness), no ongoing idda so no tuhma; in the second case, idda ongoing so tuhma exists. Abu Hanifa: The prior marriage creates intimacy and collusion regardless of idda; the couple only revealed the divorce in illness, which is suspicious.
Abu Hanifa critiques the restriction of tuhma to the idda period.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the inheritance share would have been $5,000 and the bequest is $10,000: under Abu Hanifa, she gets $5,000 in both cases; under Zufar, she gets $10,000 in both; under Sahibayn, she gets $10,000 in the first case and $5,000 in the second. This difference affects estate planning.
The dispute is well-known and the mufta bihi often follows Abu Hanifa.

[٣] قوله: على ثلاث؛ وكذا لو توافقا على إيقاع واحد أو اثنين، ومضي العدة. [٤] قوله: ومضي العدة؛ عطف على قوله: «ثلاث»؛ أي وقع التصادق على كل من الأمرين: وقوع الثلاث حال الصحة وانقضاء العدة. وقيد به ليظهر خلاف الصاحبين فيه، فإنه لو لم يتصادقا على مضي العدة فلها الأقل اتفاقاً، قال ابن الهمام في فتح القدير: هاتان مسألتان ما إذا تصادقا في مرض موته على طلاقها وانقضاء عدتها قبل المرض، وما إذا أنشأ الطلاق ثلاثاً في مرضها بسؤالها، ثم أقر لها بمال أو أوصى لها بوصية. ثم أقر لها بدين، أو أوصى بشيء، فلها الأقل منه، ومن الإرث. (ثم أقر لها بدين، أو أوصى بشيء، فلها الأقل منه، ومن الإرث): أي إن كان المقر به أو الموصى به أقل من الإرث فلها ذلك، وإن كان الإرث أقل فلها الإرث. فعند أبي حنيفة: لها الأقل من الميراث ومن كل من الوصية والمقر به في الفصلين. وقال زفر: لها تمام المقر به والموصى به في الفصلين. وقالا: في الأول كقول زفر، وفي الثاني كقول أبي حنيفة. لزفر: إن المانع من صحة الإقرار والوصية الإرث، وقد بطل بتصادقهما على انقضاء العدة قبل الموت في الأولى، وسؤالها في الثانية، فيجب اعتبار موجبهما. قلنا: ذلك لو لم تكن تهمة، لكنها ثابتة، غير أنهما قالا: إنما هي ثابتة في الثانية لا الأولى؛ وذلك لأن ثبوت التهمة به باطن، فأدير على مظنتها، وذلك قيام العدة، وهو في الثانية لا الأولى، فوجب تفصيلنا بين الفصلين. ولأبي حنيفة: أن قصر سبب التهمة على العدة ممنوع، بل هي ثابتة أيضاً نظراً إلى تقدم النكاح المفيد للألفة والشفقة وإرادة إيصال الخير، ولما لم يظهرا ما تصادقا عليه إلا في مرضه كانا متهمين في المواضعة لينفتح باب الإقرار والوصية، وهذه التهمة إنما تتحقق في حق الورثة. [١] قوله: ثم أقر لها بدين؛ بأن قال: كذا من دينها علي، وكذا لو أقر لها بعين من ماله بأنه لها. [٢] قوله: أو أوصى؛ أي أوصى بأن تعطى هي بعد موته قدر معين من تركته [٣] قوله: فلها؛ أي ليس لها جميع ما أقر لها أو أوصى لها، بل لها أقل الأمرين: الميراث والمقر به أو الموصى به؛ فإن كان نصيبه من ميراثه أقل مما أقر به أو أوصى به أخذت ذلك، وإن كان المقر به أو الموصى به أقل من نصيب الميراث أخذت ذلك. وذلك لأنها وإن صارت أجنبية عنه بتصادقهما على الطلاق وانقضاء العدة فلا ميراث لها، ويصح الإقرار والوصية لها بأي قدر كان، لكن الموضع موضع تهمة، فلا.
His saying: 'and if the spouses mutually confirm' – meaning the agreement of the wife and the husband who is sick with a fatal illness on the occurrence of three divorces in health, and on the completion of the waiting period, such that the husband says in his fatal illness: 'I divorced you three times while I was healthy, and your waiting period expired,' and she affirms him, or the wife says: 'You divorced me three times while you were healthy, and my waiting period expired,' and he affirms her. [3] His saying: 'on three' – similarly if they agree on one or two divorces and the passing of the waiting period. [4] His saying: 'and the passing of the waiting period' is a conjunction to his saying 'three' i.e., the mutual confirmation occurred on both matters: the occurrence of three divorces in health and the completion of the waiting period. It is qualified by this to show the disagreement of the two companions (Sahibayn) therein, for if they did not mutually confirm the passing of the waiting period, then she takes the lesser by agreement. Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: These are two cases: when they mutually confirm in his fatal illness her divorce and the completion of her waiting period before the illness, and when he initiated the three divorces in her illness at her request, then he acknowledged a debt to her or made a bequest to her. Then he acknowledged a debt to her, or bequeathed something, so she takes the lesser of it and the inheritance. (Then he acknowledged a debt to her, or bequeathed something, so she takes the lesser of it and the inheritance): i.e., if the acknowledged or bequeathed amount is less than the inheritance, she takes that; if the inheritance is less, she takes the inheritance. According to Abu Hanifa: she takes the lesser of the inheritance and each of the bequest and acknowledged debt in both cases. Zufar said: she takes the full acknowledged and bequeathed amount in both cases. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: in the first case like Zufar's statement, and in the second like Abu Hanifa's statement. For Zufar: The impediment to the validity of acknowledgment and bequest is inheritance, and it has been nullified by their mutual confirmation of the completion of the waiting period before death in the first case, and by her request in the second, so their consequences must be considered. We say: That would be if there were no suspicion, but it is established, except that they (the two companions) said: It is only established in the second case, not the first. This is because the establishment of suspicion is something internal, so it is attached to its apparent indication, which is the existence of the waiting period, and that is present in the second case, not the first, so our distinction between the two cases is necessary. For Abu Hanifa: that the restriction of the cause of suspicion to the waiting period is not accepted; rather, it is also established considering the prior marriage which produced intimacy and compassion and the desire to do good, and since they did not manifest what they mutually confirmed except in his illness, they are suspected of collusion to open the door of acknowledgment and bequest. This suspicion is only realized with respect to the heirs. [1] His saying: 'then he acknowledged a debt to her' – such as saying: such amount of her debt is owed by me, and similarly if he acknowledged a specific asset of his property as belonging to her. [2] His saying: 'or bequeathed' – i.e., he bequeathed that she be given after his death a specific amount from his estate. [3] His saying: 'so she takes' – i.e., she does not take all that he acknowledged or bequeathed to her, but she takes the lesser of the two matters: the inheritance and the acknowledged or bequeathed amount. If her share of the inheritance is less than what he acknowledged or bequeathed, she takes that; if the acknowledged or bequeathed amount is less than the inheritance share, she takes that. That is because, even though she became a stranger to him by their mutual confirmation of divorce and completion of the waiting period, so she has no inheritance, and acknowledgment and bequest to her are valid in any amount, yet the context is one of suspicion, so...
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the divorce of a sick person. It addresses the scenario where the spouses mutually confirm (tasāduq) that the husband had divorced her three times while healthy, and that her waiting period (idda) has expired. This confirmation occurs during the husband's fatal illness. The ruling concerns the validity of a subsequent acknowledgment (iqrār) of debt or bequest (wasiyya) by the husband to the wife. Since they confirm that the divorce occurred in health and idda ended before the illness, she becomes a stranger (ajnabiyya) to him for inheritance purposes, so she is not an heir. However, the husband may wish to give her something. The dispute among Hanafi imams is about the extent of what she can receive. Abu Hanifa holds that she takes the lesser of the inheritance share (if she were an heir) and the acknowledged/bequeathed amount. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differentiate: in the case of mutual confirmation of divorce and idda before illness, they agree with Zufar that she takes the full acknowledgment/bequest (since the obstacle of inheritance is removed by the confirmation of idda before death), but in the case where she requested the divorce in her illness, they agree with Abu Hanifa that she takes the lesser. Zufar holds she takes the full amount in both cases. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the potential for collusion (tuhma) is still present because the couple may have conspired to allow the husband to give her more than her inheritance share, and this conspiracy is suspected due to the continued intimacy and affection from the prior marriage. The two companions argue that the suspicion is only present when the idda is ongoing, so in the first case (idda already expired before illness) there is no suspicion, but in the second case (divorce in illness at her request) the suspicion remains. Abu Hanifa counters that the suspicion is not limited to the idda; it exists due to the prior marriage bond itself. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated in the text, but the later practice may follow Abu Hanifa's view. The text ends abruptly with 'فلا' (so...), likely continuing with the conclusion that the suspicion prevents the full effect.

Key Terms
تصادق (taṣāduq): Mutual confirmation between spouses regarding a past event, here the occurrence of divorce in health and completion of idda.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of a debt or right owed to another; in this context, the husband's statement that he owes the wife a sum.
وصية (waṣiyya): Bequest made by the sick husband to his divorced wife, subject to the same limitation as iqrār in this context.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion of collusion or fraud; in this context, the suspicion that the couple conspired to deprive the true heirs by fabricating the divorce and idda completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what does a wife receive when her sick husband acknowledges a debt to her after mutual confirmation that he divorced her in health and her idda ended?
A) The full amount of the acknowledged debt.
B) The lesser of the inheritance share and the acknowledged debt.
C) The inheritance share only.
D) Nothing, because the acknowledgment is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, suspicion of collusion limits a terminally ill husband's bequest or acknowledgment to his divorced wife, even after mutual confirmation of divorce and completed idda, reflecting careful protection of heirs' rights.

The Lesser of Two Amounts: Suspicion of Collusion in a Sick Husband's Admission to His Divorced Wife
Dispute over amount due to divorced wife when husband admits debt or bequests in illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a terminally ill husband admits a debt or bequests to his divorced wife, and explain the underlying rationale of tuhma (suspicion of collusion).

Core Idea
A divorced wife receives the lesser of her inheritance share and the admitted/bequeathed amount due to suspicion of collusion.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a husband who, during his terminal illness, divorces his wife and subsequently either admits a debt to her or makes a bequest. The central question is: how much is she entitled to? The Hanafi school resolves this through the principle of tuhma (suspicion of collusion), which restricts the amount to the lesser of two figures to protect the rights of other heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and general ruling
Read the passage to understand the situation: a husband divorces his wife in marad al-mawt, then admits a debt or bequests to her. The general ruling is that she takes the lesser of the admitted/bequeathed amount and her hypothetical inheritance share.
The inheritance share is what she would have inherited had the marriage continued until death.
2
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa, Zufar, and the Sahibayn
Note that Abu Hanifa applies the lesser rule uniformly in both cases (whether the admission is made during 'idda or after). Zufar gives the full amount in both cases. The Sahibayn distinguish: full amount if during 'idda, lesser if after.
The two cases are: (1) admission/bequest while 'idda is still running, (2) after 'idda has ended.
3
Analyze the arguments
Zufar argues that the impediment of inheritance is removed by mutual agreement that 'idda ended (first case) or by her request (second case), so the admission/bequest should be fully effective. Abu Hanifa responds that suspicion of collusion arises from the prior marriage itself, not just the 'idda, so both cases are tainted.
The Sahibayn's distinction hinges on the presumption that during 'idda, the marriage bond is still fresh, reducing suspicion.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the wife always receives the lesser of the two amounts. This prevents collusion to deprive other heirs.
The practical difference: under Zufar, the wife could receive a larger amount even exceeding her inheritance share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أقر لها بدين، أو أوصى بشيء، فلها الأقل منه، ومن الإرث: أي إن كان المقر به، أو الموصى به أقل من الإرث، فلها ذلك، وإن كان الإرث أقل، فلها الإرث. فعند أبي حنيفة : لها الأقل من الميراث ومن كل من الوصية والمقر به في الفصلين. وقال زفر : لها تمام المقر به، والموصى به في الفصلين. وقالا : في الأول كقول زفر، وفي الثاني كقول أبي حنيفة. لزفر : إن المانع من صحة الإقرار والوصية الإرث، وقد بطل بتصادقهما على انقضاء العدة قبل الموت في الأولى، وسؤالها في الثانية، فيجب اعتبار موجبهما. قلنا : ذلك لو لم تكن تهمة، لكنها ثابتة، غير أنهما قالا : إنما هي ثابتة في الثانية لا الأولى؛ وذلك لأن ثبوت التهمة به باطن، فأدير على مظنتها، وذلك قيام العدة، وهو في الثانية لا الأولى، فوجب تفصيلنا بين الفصلين. ولأبي حنيفة : أن قصر سبب التهمة على العدة ممنوع، بل هي ثابتة أيضاً، نظراً إلى تقدم النكاح المفيد للألفة والشفقة وإرادة إيصال الخير، ولما لم يظهرا ما تصادقا عليه إلا في مرضه كانا متهمين في المواضعة، لينفتح باب الإقرار والوصية، وهذه التهمة إنما تتحقق في حق الورثة.
Then if he admits a debt to her, or bequeaths something, she takes the lesser of the two: that [admission/bequest] and the inheritance. That is, if the admitted amount or bequest is less than the inheritance, she takes that; if the inheritance is less, she takes the inheritance. According to Abu Hanifa: she takes the lesser of the inheritance and each of the bequest and the admission in both cases. Zufar said: she takes the full admitted and bequeathed amount in both cases. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: in the first case like Zufar, and in the second like Abu Hanifa. Zufar's argument: the impediment to the validity of admission and bequest is the inheritance, and it has ceased due to their mutual agreement that the 'idda ended before death in the first case, and her request in the second, so their implications must be considered. We responded: That would be if there were no suspicion, but suspicion is established. However, they (the Sahibayn) said: suspicion is established only in the second case, not the first; because the proof of suspicion is hidden, so it is made contingent upon its presumption, which is the existence of the 'idda, and that exists in the second case not the first, so our distinction between the two cases is necessary. Abu Hanifa's argument: restricting the cause of suspicion to the 'idda is untenable; rather, suspicion is also established considering the prior marriage that produced intimacy, compassion, and desire to convey good. Since they did not reveal what they agreed upon except during his illness, they are both suspected of collusion to open the door for admission and bequest. And this suspicion exists against the heirs.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a woman divorced by her husband during his terminal illness (marad al-mawt). If after the divorce he acknowledges a debt (iqrar) in her favor or makes a bequest (wasiyya) to her, what amount is she entitled to? The general ruling is that she takes the lesser of two amounts: (1) her inheritance share had the marriage still existed, and (2) the amount admitted or bequeathed. The wisdom behind this is to prevent collusion (tuhma) between the divorcing couple to deprive the other heirs. Abu Hanifa holds this view uniformly in both scenarios: whether the admission/bequest occurs while she is in her 'idda (first case, where she still could inherit if she died in 'idda) or after the 'idda has ended (second case). Zufar argues that since the impediment of inheritance is removed by mutual agreement that the 'idda ended (first case) or by her request for divorce (second case), the admission/bequest should be fully effective. The Sahibayn distinguish between the two cases: they agree with Zufar when the admission/bequest is made during the 'idda (because the 'idda's continued existence rebuts the suspicion of collusion), but they side with Abu Hanifa when the 'idda has ended (because the parties could have colluded to make the admission only after the 'idda). Abu Hanifa's response is that the suspicion arises from the marriage itself (prior intimacy), not solely from the 'idda, so both cases are tainted by the same suspicion. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is the most precautionary against collusion and protecting the heirs' rights.

Key Terms
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion of collusion between the divorcing parties to deprive other heirs of their rightful inheritance.
إقرار (iqrar): An admission of a debt owed to another, which in sickness may be restricted due to tuhma.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest made in terminal illness, which cannot exceed one-third of the estate unless heirs consent, and is subject to tuhma when made to a former spouse.
ميراث (miraath): The share a wife would have inherited had the marriage not ended by divorce during terminal illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A terminally ill man divorces his wife, then after her 'idda ends, he admits a debt of $10,000 to her. Her inheritance share had the marriage continued would be $6,000. How much does she receive according to Abu Hanifa?
A) $10,000
B) $6,000
C) $16,000
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, to prevent collusion, a divorced wife in marad al-mawt receives only the lesser of her inheritance share and the amount admitted or bequeathed.
