Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
The Lesser of Inheritance and Bequest in Sick Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on grammatical interpretation and ruling for sick divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a wife divorced by a terminally ill husband receives the lesser of what is bequeathed or acknowledged to her and her inheritance, and distinguish the agreed-upon case from the disputed intra-Hanafi case.

Core Idea
When a sick man divorces, the wife gets whichever is smaller — bequest or inheritance — even if Zufar disagrees.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies a grammatical nuance in the matn and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute. The key is interpreting the phrase 'الأقل منه ومن الإرث' not as a comparative but as a selection between two alternatives. The commentator defends the majority position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn against Zufar's dissent, emphasizing the suspicion (tuhma) of collusion that would otherwise deprive other heirs.

Guided Path
1
Parse the grammatical issue
Identify the function of 'min' and 'waw' in the phrase 'الأقل منه ومن الإرث'. According to the commentator, 'min' is for bayan (clarification), not as part of a comparative; the 'waw' actually means 'or' (aw). This interpretation is necessary to avoid the incorrect meaning that she gets something less than each of the two.
If 'min' were a connected particle, the ruling would be that the obligatory amount is less than each one, which is impossible if they are different.
2
Understand the substantive rule
The wife receives the lesser of two amounts: (1) what is bequeathed or acknowledged to her, and (2) her inheritance share. The practical effect is to prevent her from profiting at the expense of other heirs.
This rule applies only when the divorce occurs during the husband's terminal illness (marad al-mawt).
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
The passage compares two cases: (a) the husband divorces his wife without her request (the first scenario, which involves disagreement among the imams), and (b) the wife directly asks for the divorce (the second scenario, which is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn). In both, the same rule of giving the lesser applies, but the first case had ikhtilaf.
The commentator uses the agreed case to strengthen the ruling for the disputed case via comparison (tashbih).
4
Identify Zufar's dissent
Zufar disagrees with the majority in the second scenario. His exact position is not detailed, but the commentator implies he would not apply the 'lesser' rule, possibly giving the wife the full bequest or acknowledgment.
The majority view is relied upon (mufta bihi).
5
Note the practical consequence
Under the majority view, if the wife's inheritance is small, she receives only that small amount; under Zufar's view, she might receive more, potentially harming other heirs.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant: the difference directly affects the distribution of the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق طلاق المريض
واعلم أن حرف من ؛ في قوله : فلها الأقل منه ومن الإرث ؛ ليست صلة لأفعل التفضيل إذ لو كان يجب أن يكون الواجب أقل من كل واحد منهما، وليس كذلك، بل حرف من للبيان، وأفعل التفضيل استعمل باللام، فيجب أن يقال : أو من الإرث ؛ لأنه لما قال : الأقل ؛ بَيْنَ الأقل بأحدهما، وصلة الأقل محذوف، وهو من الآخر : أي فلها أحدهما الذي هو أقل من الآخر، فيكون الواو بمعنى : أو يصدقان في حق باقي الورثة، فلعلهما توافقا عليه ليصل إليهما أكثر مما يصل إليها إرثاً حال بقاء الزوجية ؛ إذ لا تصح الوصية لوارث، ولا الإقرار له في مرض الموت.
(1)
ثم ما تأخذه له شبهة الميراث، فلو هلك شيء من التركة قبل القسمة كان على الكل، ولو طلبت أخذ الدراهم والتركةُ عروض، لم يكن لها، وله شبه بالدين، حتى كان للورثة أن يعطوها من غير التركة، مؤاخذة لها بزعمها أنّ ما تأخذه دين لا ميراث. كذا في «الفتح».
[١] قوله : واعلم ... الخ ؛ توضيحه : أنّ الغرض هاهنا أنها تستحق أقل الأمرين المقرّ به أو الموصى به والميراث، يعني تعطى ما كان أقل من الآخر، فإن كان الميراث أقل من المقرّ به أو الموصى به فلها ذلك، وإن كان أحدهما أقل من الإرث فلها ذلك، وهذا المقصود لا يفهم من عبارة المتن إلا بأن تكون «من» في الموضعين للبيان، و«الواو» بمعنى «أو»، وصلة الأقل محذوفة، يعني من الآخر.
والمعنى: فلها الموصى به الأقلّ من الميراث أو الميراث الأقل من الموصى به، ولا يجوز أن تكون الواو للجمع ؛ إذ يصير المعنى حينئذ فلها الميراث والموصى به اللذان هما أقل أحدهما، ولا يجوز أيضاً : أن تكون من صلة الأقل سواء كانت «الواو» للجمع، أو بمعنى «أو» ؛ لأنه يصير المعنى حينئذ ، فلها الأقل من كل واحد منهما، أو فلها الأقل من ا، وهو يدل على أنّ الأقل شيء خارج منهما، وليس كذلك.
[٢]قوله : فيكون ؛ تفريع على ما فُهِمَ سابقاً أنه كان على المصنف له أن يأتي بـ«أو»، فإن المقام مقتض له لا للواو، والغرض منه إصلاح كلامه على طبق مرامه
كمَن طُلقت ثلاثاً بأمرها في مرضه ، ثم أقر أو أوصى أو يكون الواو على معناها، لكن لا يراد بها المجموع، بل يراد الأقل الذي هو الإرث تارة، والموصى به أُخرى، فيكون الواو للجمع، وهو أن الأقلية ثابتة ، لكن بحسب زمانين.
[١] كمَن طُلِّقَتْ ثلاثاً بأمرها في مرضه، ثمّ أقر أو أوصى) ؛ فإنَّ لها الأقل [۳] من ذلك، ومن الإرث في قولهم جميعا.
بطريقين :
أحدهما : أن تكون «الواو» في قوله : «ومن الإرث» بمعنى «أو»، فكثيراً ما تجيء الواو بمعنى «أو»، وحينئذ يتضح المقصود ، ولا يخل فيه إيراد «الواو». وثانيهما : أن تكون «الواو» للجمع، لكن لاختلاف الزمان، حتى لا يلزم كونُ كل واحدٍ أقل من الآخر في زمان واحد ؛ لاستحالته، فإن أقلية أحدهما مستلزمة لأكثرية الآخر، بل يكون المقصود كون الإرث أقل من المقرّ به أو الموصى به تارة ، وكون أحدهما أقل من الإرث تارة.
[1] قوله : كمن ؛ تشبيه للمسألة الأولى بالمسألة الثانية في الحكم : وهو أن لها أحد الأمرين، وهو أقلهما ، ولَمَّا كانت الأولى اختلافية والثانية اتفاقية كما مر ذكره ، ناسب تشبيه الأولى بالثانية دون العكس، فإنّ المشبه به يُستحسن أن يكون أقوى وأوضح. وحاصل هذه المسألة : أنه طلبت في مرضه منه الطلاق ثلاثاً ففعل، ثم أقر لها بشيء أو أوصى بشيء، فالتهمة حينئذ موجودة مستحكمة، فلا يعتبر فعلهما في حق باقي الورثة ، بل يكون الأقل من الآخر إرثاً كان أو المقربه أو الموصى به.
[٢] قوله : فإنّ لها ...الخ ؛ اقتدى الشارح له في عنوان البيان في هذا المقام بالمصنف ، حيث أتى بكلمة أتى بها المصنّف له سابقاً، مع تصريحه سابقاً أنّ الواجب كان الإتيان بـ «أو» بدل «الواو»، وكان الأولى له أن يأتي هاهنا بـ«أو»، فإنّه لا تقليد في الباطل، وغير المستحسن.
[٣] قوله : في قولهم ؛ أي أئمتنا ، وأشار به إلى وقوع الخلاف في المسألة الأولى، وقد مرّ منّا ذكره، وكان الأولى له أن ينبه على قدر منه سابقاً ليستحسن هاهنا قوله في قولهم جميعاً ، ثمّ المراد بالاتفاق هاهنا اتفاق أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه ، وإلا فزفر له
Book of Divorce: Divorce of the Sick Person
Know that the letter 'min' in His statement: 'She gets the lesser of it and of the inheritance' is not a connected particle for the superlative adjective, because if it were, it would necessitate that the obligatory amount is less than each one of them, and it is not so. Rather, the letter 'min' is for clarification, and the superlative adjective is used with the lam, so it should be said: 'or from the inheritance' because when he said 'the lesser', he specified the lesser by one of them, and the connection of 'the lesser' is omitted, and it is 'from the other', meaning: she gets one of them that is less than the other. Thus the waw is in the meaning of 'or'. Both statements are true regarding the rest of the heirs, perhaps they agreed upon it so that more reaches them than reaches her as inheritance during the state of marriage, because a bequest to an heir is invalid, nor is an acknowledgment for him valid during terminal illness.
(1)
Then what she takes has the semblance of inheritance, so if something from the estate perishes before division, it is upon all. And if she demands to take dirhams while the estate consists of goods, she does not have that right, and it has the semblance of a debt, such that the heirs may give her from outside the estate, holding her responsible for her claim that what she takes is a debt, not inheritance. Thus in al-Fath.
[1] His statement: 'Know... etc.' Its clarification: The purpose here is that she deserves the lesser of the two matters: what is acknowledged or bequeathed, and the inheritance. That is, she is given whatever is less than the other. If the inheritance is less than what is acknowledged or bequeathed, she gets that; if one of them is less than the inheritance, she gets that. This intended meaning is not understood from the text of the matn except by making 'min' in both places for clarification, and the 'waw' in the meaning of 'or', and the connection of 'the lesser' is omitted, i.e., 'from the other'.
The meaning: She gets the bequest that is less than the inheritance or the inheritance that is less than the bequest. It is not permissible for the waw to indicate conjunction, because then the meaning would become: she gets the inheritance and the bequest which are the lesser of the two. It is also not permissible for 'min' to be a connected particle, whether the waw is for conjunction or in the meaning of 'or', because then the meaning would become: she gets the lesser of each one of them, or she gets the lesser of... which indicates that the lesser is something external to them, and it is not so.
[2] His statement: 'Thus it becomes' is a subdivision based on what was understood earlier, that the author should have used 'or', because the context requires it, not the waw, and the purpose is to correct his statement according to his intention.
Like one who was divorced three times by her request during his illness, then he acknowledged or bequeathed, or the waw is upon its meaning, but the collective is not intended, rather the lesser is intended, which is the inheritance sometimes, and the bequest other times, so the waw is for conjunction, with the lesser being established, but according to two times.
[1] Like one who was divorced three times by her request during his illness, then he acknowledged or bequeathed. So she gets the lesser of that and of the inheritance, in all of their statements.
In two ways:
One: That the waw in his statement 'and from the inheritance' is in the meaning of 'or', for often the waw comes in the meaning of 'or', and then the intended meaning becomes clear, and the use of the waw does not impair it. The second: That the waw is for conjunction, but due to difference in time, so that it does not necessitate that each one is less than the other at one time, because that is impossible, since the lesser of one entails the greater of the other. Rather, the intended meaning is that the inheritance is less than the acknowledged or bequeathed sometimes, and that one of them is less than the inheritance at other times.
[1] His statement: 'Like...' is a comparison of the first issue to the second issue in the ruling: that she has one of the two matters, namely the lesser of them. Since the first involves disagreement and the second involves agreement as mentioned previously, it is appropriate to compare the first to the second and not the opposite, because what is being compared should ideally be stronger and clearer. The summary of this issue: She asked him during his illness for divorce three times, and he did it, then he acknowledged something for her or bequeathed something, so the suspicion is present and strong, so his action is not considered regarding the rest of the heirs; rather, the lesser of the other is taken, whether it be inheritance or the acknowledged or bequeathed.
[2] His statement: 'For her... etc.' The commentator followed the author in the title of the discussion in this place, where he used the word that the author used previously, despite his earlier statement that the obligation was to use 'or' instead of 'waw', and it would have been better for him to use 'or' here, for there is no emulation in falsehood, and that is not commendable.
[3] His statement: 'In their statements' i.e., our imams, and he pointed to the occurrence of disagreement in the first issue, which we have mentioned previously. It would have been better for him to alert to some of it earlier to make his statement here 'in all of their statements' commendable. Then, by agreement here is meant the agreement of Abu Hanifa and his two companions; otherwise, Zufar has a different opinion.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling that when a sick man divorces his wife, she gets the lesser of two amounts: whatever he acknowledged (iqrar) or bequeathed (wasiyya) to her, and her share of inheritance (mirath) if he dies. The commentator, from the Hanafi school, begins by clarifying a grammatical point in the original text (matn). The phrase 'فَلَها الأقل منه ومن الإرث' (she gets the lesser of it and of the inheritance) uses the letters 'min' and 'waw' in a specific way. The commentator argues that 'min' here is not part of a comparative structure (like 'less than'), but rather for bayan (clarification), and the 'waw' actually means 'or' (aw). This is because the intended meaning is that she receives whichever is less: either the bequest/acknowledgment or her inheritance, not a combined amount. The commentator then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute. While Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani are in agreement on the ruling in a second scenario (where the woman directly asks for divorce in her husband's illness and then he makes a bequest), Zufar disagrees. The passage compares this agreed case to the first case (where the divorce is not requested by her), showing that the same rule of giving the lesser applies, but the first case involved ikhtilaf (disagreement) among the imams. The commentator critiques the original author's wording for using 'waw' instead of 'aw', but provides two interpretive ways to still reach the correct meaning. The passage also explains that what the wife takes has a semblance of inheritance (shubhat al-mirath), not actual inheritance, so if the estate perishes, it is shared by all heirs, and the wife cannot demand specific types of property if they are not in the estate. This is due to the suspicion (tuhma) that the husband might favor her at the expense of other heirs, similar to the rule that bequests to heirs are invalid.

Key Terms
طلاق المريض (talaq al-marid): Divorce pronounced by a person who is terminally ill, subject to special rules regarding inheritance and bequests due to suspicion of depriving heirs.
الأقل من الإرث والموصى به (al-aqall min al-irath wa al-musa bih): The legal principle that the divorced wife in a sick man's case receives whichever is smaller: her inheritance or what is bequeathed/acknowledged to her.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or right, here by the sick husband to his divorced wife; treated with suspicion in terminal illness.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion or presumption of collusion; in this context, that the sick husband may favor the divorced wife to the detriment of other heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a terminally ill man divorcing his wife at her request, and then bequeathing her something, what does she receive according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
A) The bequeathed amount in full
B) The inheritance share in full
C) The lesser of the bequest and the inheritance
D) Both the bequest and the inheritance together

Key Takeaway
The wife of a terminally ill man who divorces her receives the smaller of whatever he bequeaths or acknowledges to her and her inheritance, based on the majority Hanafi view.

Woman Divorced at Her Request: Iqrar and Inheritance
Commentary on a ruling with linguistic and analogical proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a woman divorced thrice at her request during terminal illness and apply the principle of tuhma to determine whether she receives the iqrar/wasiyyah or inheritance.

Core Idea
A wife who requested divorce during illness cannot take more than the lesser of her inheritance and what her husband gave her — fraud suspicion limits her.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah examines a specific case where a wife, after requesting and receiving a triple divorce during her husband's terminal illness, is later acknowledged a debt or bequeathed something. The ruling — that she receives only the lesser amount — is based on the strong suspicion (tuhma) of collusion to defraud other heirs. The commentator not only states the ruling but also provides two linguistic interpretations to reconcile the wording and draws an analogy to an agreed-upon case, while noting a dissenting opinion from Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the legal outcome for the woman: she takes the lesser of the iqrar/wasiyyah amount and her inheritance share.
This is stated clearly at the beginning: 'fainna laha al-aqall min dhalik wa min al-irth'.
2
Understand the proof: linguistic interpretation
The commentator offers two ways to read the conjunction 'waw' in the matn: either it means 'or' (aw) or it applies to different times. Both avoid the logical impossibility of both amounts being less simultaneously.
This shows Hanafi usul principles at work in clarifying ambiguous texts.
3
Analyze the analogy (tashbih)
The case is compared to an earlier agreed-upon case (the 'second issue'). The comparison is appropriate because the comparandum (the agreed case) is stronger and clearer, establishing the same ruling: the woman takes only one of the two, the lesser.
The analogy is based on the shared illa of tuhma.
4
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
While Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad agree on this ruling, Zufar disagreed. The commentator references al-Hidayah for details. The agreement of the three imams is the mufta bihi position.
This illustrates that even within the Hanafi school, there can be legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
Use the principle of tuhma to determine when a transaction during terminal illness is restricted. The key is whether there is strong suspicion of collusion between the spouses to deprive other heirs.
Apply to similar scenarios, e.g., gifts or sales during marad al-mawt.

بطريقين :

Like the one who was divorced three times at her command during his illness, then he acknowledged (a debt) or bequeathed (something to her); then she has the lesser of that and the inheritance in the opinion of all of them (the imams). In two ways: One is that the 'waw' in his statement 'and from the inheritance' means 'or', for often the waw comes in the meaning of 'or', and then the intended meaning becomes clear, and the use of the waw does not spoil it. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling regarding a woman who is divorced three times at her own request during her husband's terminal illness, and then the husband either acknowledges a debt to her or bequeaths something to her. The ruling states that she takes the lesser of the two amounts: either the acknowledged/bequeathed amount or her inheritance share. The commentary provides two linguistic interpretations for the wording of the original matn: either the 'waw' (و) in 'wa min al-irth' means 'or' (أو), so it means 'or from the inheritance'; or it is used for combination but with reference to different times, preventing the logical impossibility of both being less at the same time. The author then explains that this case is analogous to a previously agreed-upon case (the 'second issue'), highlighting that the first case involves disagreement (between Abu Hanifa and his companions on one side and Zufar on the other? Actually, the text says 'in the opinion of all of them' refers to Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, while Zufar disagreed). The ruling is based on the principle of preventing fraud (tuhma) against the other heirs, so only the lesser amount is valid. The commentary also criticizes the original author for using 'waw' instead of 'aw', considering it a mistake not to be blindly followed.

Key Terms
الواو بمعنى أو (al-waw bi-ma'na aw): The use of the conjunction 'wa' (and) to mean 'or' (أو) in certain contexts.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of fraud or collusion between the husband and wife to deprive other heirs of their rights.
تشبيه (tashbih): Analogical comparison between two cases for the purpose of extending a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The lesser of the iqrar/wasiyyah and the inheritance

Key Takeaway
A woman who requested divorce during her husband's terminal illness cannot take more than the lesser of her inheritance and any iqrar or wasiyyah from him, due to the principle of tuhma.

Inheritance in Conditional Divorce During Death Illness
Intra-Hanafi analysis of inheritance in conditional divorce during death illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the inheritance ruling for a wife divorced conditionally during the husband's death illness, distinguish between the three categories of conditions, and explain the Zufar dispute on the role of intent.

Core Idea
In death illness, a wife inherits from conditional divorce unless the husband had no intent to flee.

This lesson unpacks the intricate rules of inheritance when a husband divorces his wife conditionally during a fatal illness (maraḍ al-mawt). The central concern is preventing the husband from deliberately depriving his wife of inheritance (farr). The Hanafi school classifies conditions into three types – celestial/stranger's act, husband's own act, and wife's act – and applies nuanced rulings based on the timing of the conditional statement (taʿlīq) and the degree of control. An intra-Hanafi disagreement with Zufar adds depth, highlighting the importance of intent.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the principle of farr
Understand that farr (fleeing) refers to a husband deliberately divorcing his wife during death illness to deny her inheritance. The rulings are designed to counteract such evasion.
Intent is key: legal consequences alone do not constitute farr.
2
Identify the three condition categories
The passage divides conditions into: (1) celestial occurrence or stranger's action, (2) husband's own action, (3) wife's action. Each has distinct rules.
Also note the timing factor: taʿlīq in health vs. illness.
3
Analyze each category's ruling
For each category, apply the rule: if both taʿlīq and condition are in illness, wife inherits unless she caused it. Exceptions arise when taʿlīq was in health (no intent to flee).
Use the eight-scenario framework from al-Hidayah.
4
Examine Zufar's disagreement
Zufar argues that a conditional divorce upon occurrence is like an immediate pronouncement, so if the condition occurs in illness, the husband becomes a fleer even if the taʿlīq was in health. The majority holds that farr requires intent at the time of taʿlīq.
This is a subtle qiyās khafī (hidden analogy) dispute.
5
Conclude with muftā bihī
The majority position (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad) is the relied-upon view: no inheritance when taʿlīq was in health and condition in illness, unless the condition was unavoidable for the wife.
Zufar's view is marjūḥ (weaker).

كتاب الطلاق طلاق المريض ولو علق الثلاث بشرط، ووجد في مرضهِ : إن علقه بمجيء وقت كرجب ، أو فعل أجنبي ترث، إلا إذا كان عَلَّقَ في صحتِه. وإن علق بفعل نفسه ترث ، سواءٌ كَانَ التعليق في مرضه أو لا ، والفعل مما له منه بد كالكلام مع الأجنبي، أو لا بد له كأكل الطعام، وصلاة الظهر، وكلام الأبوين. وإن علّق بفعلها : فإن كانا في مرضه ، والفعلُ لها منه بد لا ترث ، وإن لم يكن لها منه بد ترث. مخالف في هذه المسألة أيضاً كما فصله في «الهداية». [١]قوله : كرجب؛ - بفتحتين : علم الأحدِ الشهور الحرم الأربعة، الواقع بين جمادى الثانية وشعبان، وذلك كقوله : إذا دخلت رجب فأنت طالق. [٢] قوله : أو فعل أجنبي ؛ بالإضافة ، والمراد بالفعل ما يعم الترك، والمراد بالأجنبي معناه المتعارف ؛ أي من لا قرابة له، بل غير الزوجين ولو ولدها منه. كذا في «الدر المختار»، وحواشيه [٣] (۳) قوله : إلا ؛ يعني لو علق في صحته، ثمّ مرض الموت، ووجد ذلك الشرط فيه، وهو ما لا اختيار لأحد الزوجين فيه، فحينئذ لا ترث، ولا يكون هو به فاراً. [٤] قوله : وإن ؛ أي إن علّق الزوج طلاقها بفعل من أفعال نفسه، ووجد ذلك الشرط في مرضه ترث سواء كان تعليقه به في صحته أو مرضه، وسواء كان الفعل تما يضطر إلى ارتكابه أو لا. [0]قوله : أو لا بد له منه ؛ أي طبعاً كالأكل والشرب ونحوهما، أو شرعاً كأداء الصلاة المفروضة، والصوم، وقضاء الدين واستيفائه، وكلام الأبوين، وكذا كل ذي رحم محرم. كذا في «النهر» وإن علّق بفعلها : فإن كانا : أي التَّعليقُ والشَّرط (في مرضه، والفعل لها منه بد لا ترث ، وإن لم يكن لها منه بد ترث. [١] قوله : فإن كانا ... الخ ؛ توضيح هذه المباحث علـى مـا في «الهدايــة» وشروحها : إن الطلاق لا يخلو إما أن يعلقه الزوج بعارض سماوي كمجيء وقت أو بفعل غيرهما، أو بفعل نفسه، أو بفعلها، وكلّ وجه لا يخلو من أن يكون التعليق في الصحة والشرط في المرض، أو كلاهما في المرض، فهذه ثمان صور. وأما إن كان التعليق والشرط كلاهما في الصحة، أو التعليق في المرض والشرط في الصحة، بأن صح من مرضه ذلك ، فقد عُلم ما مرّ أنه ليس من صور الفرار، ففي الوجهين الأولين؛ أي إذا كان التعليق بمجيء الوقت، كقوله : إذا جاءَ رأس الشهر فأنت طالق ، أو بفعل الأجنبي نحو : إذا دخل فلان الدار أو صلى فلان الظهر ترث إذا كان الشرط والتعليق كلاهما في المرض ؛ لوجودِ الفرار منه ، بتعليقه الطلاق في حال تعلق حق الورثة بماله، وهو مرض الموت. وإن كان التعليق في الصحة، ووجود الشرط في المرض لم ترث، خلافاً لزفر له. له : أن المعلّق بالشرط ينزلُ عند وجوده، وهو عنده كالمنجز، فكان إيقاعاً في المرض، فيعد فاراً. ولنا : إنّ كون التعليق تطليقاً عند وجود الشرط أمر حكمي لا قصدي، ولا يصير ظالماً فاراً إلا بالقصد، وإذ ليس فليس. وفي الوجه الثالث : يعني ما إذا علّقه بفعل نفسه ترث مطلقاً، سواء كان التعليق في الصحة أو في المرض، وسواء كان الفعل تما له بُدَّ منه ؛ أي يمكن منه أن لا يرتكبه، أو كان مما لا بد منه ؛ لأنه يصير فاراً إما بالتعليق في المرض، وإما بمباشرة الشرط في المرض. فإن قلت : إذا كان الفعلُ مما لا بد منه يكون مضطراً طبعاً أو شرعاً إلى إتيانه فلا يكون إتيانه ظلماً. قطعاً. قلت : إن لم يكن له من وجود الشرط بد، فله من التعليق بفعل نفسه الكذائي به
Book of Divorce: Divorce of the Sick. And if he made the three (divorces) conditional upon a condition, and it occurred during his illness: If he made it conditional upon the arrival of a time like Rajab, or an action of a stranger, she inherits, unless he made the conditional statement in his health. And if he made it conditional upon his own action, she inherits, whether the conditional statement was during his illness or not, and whether the action is something he can avoid like speaking with a stranger, or cannot avoid like eating food, performing Zuhr prayer, and speaking to parents. And if he made it conditional upon her action: if both (the conditional statement and the condition) are during his illness and the action is something she can avoid, she does not inherit; if she cannot avoid it, she inherits. There is a disagreement in this issue as well, as detailed in al-Hidayah. [1] His statement: like Rajab – with two fatha vowels – is the name of one of the four sacred months, which falls between Jumada al-Thaniyya and Sha'ban, such as when he says: 'If Rajab enters, you are divorced.' [2] His statement: or an action of a stranger – with idafa (construct), and by action is meant what includes omitting, and by stranger is meant its conventional meaning: i.e., someone who has no relationship, rather other than the spouses, even if he is her child from him. This is as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its glosses. [3] His statement: except – meaning if he made the conditional statement in his health, then fell into death illness, and that condition occurred therein, which is something in which neither spouse has a choice, then she does not inherit, and he is not considered fleeing by it. [4] His statement: and if – i.e., if the husband made her divorce conditional upon an action of his own, and that condition occurred during his illness, she inherits, whether he made the conditional statement during his health or his illness, and whether the action is something he is compelled to do or not. [0] His statement: or cannot avoid – i.e., naturally like eating, drinking, etc., or legally like performing the obligatory prayer, fasting, repaying debt and collecting it, and speaking to parents, and likewise every mahram relative. This is as in al-Nahr. And if he made it conditional upon her action: if both (the conditional statement and the condition) are during his illness and the action is something she can avoid, she does not inherit; if she cannot avoid it, she inherits. [1] His statement: 'if both' etc. – clarification of these investigations according to what is in al-Hidayah and its commentaries: Divorce is either that the husband makes it conditional upon a celestial occurrence like the arrival of a time, or upon an action of someone other than them, or upon his own action, or upon her action. Each category is either that the conditional statement is in health and the condition in illness, or both in illness. So these are eight scenarios. As for when both the conditional statement and the condition are in health, or the conditional statement in illness and the condition in health such that he recovered from that illness, it is known from what has passed that these are not cases of fleeing. In the first two ways: i.e., when the conditional statement is upon the arrival of a time, such as saying 'When the beginning of the month comes, you are divorced', or upon an action of a stranger such as 'If so-and-so enters the house' or 'If so-and-so prays Zuhr', she inherits if the condition and the conditional statement are both in illness due to the presence of fleeing by his making the divorce conditional at a time when the heirs' right to his wealth is connected, i.e., death illness. And if the conditional statement is in health and the occurrence of the condition in illness, she does not inherit, contrary to Zufar. For him: the conditional (divorce) becomes effective upon occurrence, and in his view it is like an immediate pronouncement, so it would be an effectuation during illness, thus he is considered fleeing. For us: that the conditional statement being a divorce upon the occurrence of the condition is a legal and not a deliberate matter, and a person is not considered an oppressor or fleeing except by intention, and since there is no intention, it is not (considered fleeing). And in the third way: i.e., when he makes it conditional upon his own action, she inherits absolutely, whether the conditional statement is in health or illness, and whether the action is something he can avoid – i.e., he can possibly not do it – or something he cannot avoid, because he becomes a fleer either by the conditional statement in illness or by undertaking the condition in illness. If you say: when the action is something he cannot avoid, he is compelled naturally or legally to do it, so his doing it is not oppression. Definitely. I say: if he has no escape from the existence of the condition, he does have an escape from making the conditional statement upon such an action of his.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage from the book of Talaq deals with the rulings of inheritance for a wife who is divorced by a conditional pronouncement (ta'līq) during the husband's death illness (maraḍ al-mawt). The commentator, drawing from al-Hidayah and other sources, explains the scenarios and the underlying principle of fleeing (farr) from inheritance. The discussion is an intra-Hanafi dispute, with Zufar differing on one point.

The passage first presents cases where the condition is a celestial occurrence (like the arrival of Rajab) or an action of a stranger (like someone entering a house). If both the conditional statement and the condition occur during the death illness, the wife inherits because the husband is deemed to have fled by tying divorce to a condition he cannot control. However, if he made the conditional statement in health and the condition occurs in illness, she does not inherit because the husband had no intention to flee at the time of the ta'līq. Zufar disagrees, arguing that at the moment the condition occurs, it is like an immediate divorce, making him a fleer. The majority Hanafi position (us) counters that the divorce at condition is a legal consequence, not a deliberate act; fleeing requires intent.

Second, if the husband conditions divorce on his own action (like speaking or eating), the wife inherits in all cases, whether the ta'līq was in health or illness, and whether he can avoid the action or not. The reasoning is that either by making the ta'līq in illness or by performing the action in illness, he is fleeing. Even if the action is unavoidable, he could have avoided making the conditional statement on that action.

Third, if the condition is an action of the wife, the ruling depends: if both the ta'līq and condition are in illness and the wife can avoid the action, she does not inherit (because she caused it); if she cannot avoid it (e.g., menstruation), she inherits (because he fled by choosing a condition she cannot avoid).

The passage thus establishes a nuanced set of rules based on intentionality and control, all within the Hanafi school's approach to preventing unjust deprivation of inheritance.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta‘līq): A conditional pronouncement of divorce that becomes effective upon the occurrence of a specified condition.
فرار (farr): The husband's deliberate act of divorcing his wife during death illness to deprive her of inheritance, which is legally prohibited.
مرض الموت (maraḍ al-mawt): A fatal illness from which the husband is not expected to recover, during which special inheritance rules apply.
معلق بشرط (mu‘allaq bi-sharṭ): A divorce that is suspended upon the occurrence of a future condition, not immediately effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, if a husband in death illness makes a conditional divorce upon his own action (e.g., 'If I eat this food, you are divorced') and he eats, does the wife inherit?
A) Yes, because she cannot control his action.
B) Yes, because he is considered to have fled either by the taʿlīq in illness or by performing the action in illness.
C) No, because he could have avoided eating.
D) No, because the condition was his own action and he intended to flee.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances intent and control: a wife inherits from a conditional divorce unless the husband demonstrably lacked intent to flee at the time of the conditional statement.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Eight Forms of Conditional Divorce in Terminal Illness
Classification of eight forms of conditional divorce and inheritance rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any conditional divorce scenario into one of the eight forms based on type of condition and timing, and state whether the wife inherits according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The wife's inheritance in conditional divorce during terminal illness depends on whether the husband intended escape (firar) which is determined by the type of condition and timing.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah presents a comprehensive framework for analyzing conditional divorces during the husband's terminal illness. The key concept is firar: if the husband attempted to deprive his wife of inheritance, the divorce is invalid and she inherits. The scholars categorize conditional divorces into eight forms based on the type of condition (celestial, third party, husband's act, wife's act) and the timing of conditioning and condition occurrence (both in health, conditioning in health & condition in illness, both in illness). Understanding this classification is essential for determining inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of condition
Determine whether the condition is a celestial event, the act of a third party, the husband's own act, or the wife's act. Each category has its own rules.
2
Establish timing of conditioning and condition occurrence
Determine if the conditional pronouncement (ta'liq) was made while the husband was in health or terminal illness, and whether the condition occurred in health or illness. This gives four possible timing combinations.
The eight forms arise from combining the four condition types with two timing combinations (both in illness, or conditioning in health & condition in illness).
3
Apply the corresponding rule
For each combination, the passage provides the ruling on inheritance. In general, if the husband made the condition in illness or if the condition occurs in illness and he had control, firar is established and she inherits.
Exceptions and disputes are noted in the next step.
4
Note intra-Hanafi disputes
Pay attention to disagreements between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar on some scenarios, especially the celestial/third party case with conditioning in health and condition in illness.
Zufar holds that any conditional divorce occurring in illness is firar; the majority requires intent.
5
Conclude on firar
Based on the rule and preferred opinion, determine if the husband is considered an escaper (farr). If yes, the divorce is invalid and she inherits; if no, the divorce is valid and she does not inherit.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is the majority view.

٣. وإن علق بفعلها :

[١] قوله : فإن كانا ... الخ ؛ توضيح هذه المباحث علـى مـا في «الهدايــة» وشروحها : إن الطلاق لا يخلو إما أن يعلقه الزوج بعارض سماوي كمجيء وقت أو بفعل غيرهما، أو بفعل نفسه، أو بفعلها، وكلّ وجه لا يخلو من أن يكون التعليق في الصحة والشرط في المرض، أو كلاهما في المرض، فهذه ثمان صور. وأما إن كان التعليق والشرط كلاهما في الصحة، أو التعليق في المرض والشرط في الصحة، بأن صح من مرضه ذلك ، فقد عُلم ما مرّ أنه ليس من صور الفرار، ففي الوجهين الأولين؛ أي إذا كان التعليق بمجيء الوقت، كقوله : إذا جاءَ رأس الشهر فأنت طالق ، أو بفعل الأجنبي نحو : إذا دخل فلان الدار أو صلى فلان الظهر ترث إذا كان الشرط والتعليق كلاهما في المرض ؛ لوجودِ الفرار منه ، بتعليقه الطلاق في حال تعلق حق الورثة بماله، وهو مرض الموت.
وإن كان التعليق في الصحة، ووجود الشرط في المرض لم ترث، خلافاً لزفر له. له : أن المعلّق بالشرط ينزلُ عند وجوده، وهو عنده كالمنجز، فكان إيقاعاً في
المرض، فيعد فاراً.
ولنا : إنّ كون التعليق تطليقاً عند وجود الشرط أمر حكمي لا قصدي، ولا يصير ظالماً فاراً إلا بالقصد، وإذ ليس فليس.
وفي الوجه الثالث : يعني ما إذا علّقه بفعل نفسه ترث مطلقاً، سواء كان التعليق في الصحة أو في المرض، وسواء كان الفعل تما له بُدَّ منه ؛ أي يمكن منه أن لا يرتكبه، أو كان مما لا بد منه ؛ لأنه يصير فاراً إما بالتعليق في المرض، وإما بمباشرة الشرط في المرض. فإن قلت : إذا كان الفعلُ مما لا بد منه يكون مضطراً طبعاً أو شرعاً إلى إتيانه فلا يكون إتيانه ظلماً قطعاً.
قلت : إن لم يكن له من وجود الشرط بد، فله من التعليق بفعل نفسه الكذائي به
وإن كان في صحته لا ترث إلا فيما لا بُدَّ لها منه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، خلافاً لمحمد وزُفَر الله
ب. وإن كان : أي التعليق في صحته لا ترثُ إلا فيما لا بُدَّ لها منه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، خلافاً لمحمد وزُفَر ) : فإنَّها لا ترث عندهما ؛ لأنه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع بعدما تعلق حقها بماله، هذا عبارةً ((الهداية)) () ، ومعناها : إنَّ امرأة الفار إِنَّما ترثُ إِن وُجِدَ من الزوج في مرض موته صنع في إبطال حقها بعدما تعلق حقها بماله بسبب المرض، ولم يوجد ذلك الصنع ؛ لأنَّ التَّعليق كان في صحته، بل المرأة أبطلت حقها بإتيانها بذلك الفعل. وفي الوجه الرابع : وهو ما إذا علّقه بفعلها، فإن كان التعليق والشرط كلاهما في المرض لا ترث إن كان الفعل مما لها منه بد ؛ لأنه كان يمكن منها أن لا تأتي بالفعل، فلما أتت به كأنها رضيت بوقوع الطلاق، فلا يعد الزوج به فاراً، وترث إن كان الفعل مما لا بد منه، فإنّها حينئذ مضطرة إلى إتيانها ، فلا يكون ذلك دليلاً على رضاها. وإن كان التعليق في صحته والشرط في المرض لا ترث إن كان الفعل مما لها منه تما بد ؛ لأنها تصير راضية بوقوع الطلاق بإتيانه مع إمكان الاحتراز عنه، وإن كان الفعل لا بد منه ترث عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ا ؛ لأن الزوج ألجأها ؛ أي جعلها مضطرة، فينسب الفعل إليه ؛ كأنه آلة له ، فيصير فاراً به. وقال زفر ومحمد : لا ترث؛ لأنه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع في حالة المرض ؛ لكون التعليق في الصحة.
[١]قوله : ومعناها ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن إرث زوجة الفار وإبطال تطليقه في هذا الباب إنّما هو إذا وجد من الزوج فعل يصير باعثاً لوقوعه المتضمن لإبطال حقها في حالة تعلق حقها بماله ، حالة . وهو رض الموت، وفي هذه الصورة لم يوجد منه صنع كذائي ؛ لأنَّ تعليقه كان في الصحة، فينسبُ وقوع الطلاق إلى ارتكابها ذلك الفعل المعلق به. (٢) قوله : بعدما تعلّق ؛ فإنَّ الورثة يتعلّق حقهم بمال الموروث حال مرض موته ، ولهذا نهى عن الوصية والتبرع بما زاد على الثلاث في تلك الحالة إلا بإجازة الورثة.
And if he conditions it on her action: then if both are in his illness, and the action has an alternative for her, she does not inherit; and if it has no alternative for her, she inherits.
3. If conditioned on her action:
a. Then if both (i.e., conditioning and condition) are in his illness, and the action has an alternative for her, she does not inherit; and if it has no alternative for her, she inherits.
[1] His statement: 'then if both...' etc.; clarification of these discussions according to what is in al-Hidayah and its commentaries: Indeed, divorce is either that the husband conditions it on a celestial occurrence like the arrival of a time, or on the action of someone other than them, or on his own action, or on her action. Each aspect is either that the conditioning is in health and the condition in illness, or both in illness; these are eight forms. As for if both conditioning and condition are in health, or conditioning in illness and condition in health, such that he recovered from that illness, it is known from what passed that it is not from the forms of escape (firar). So in the first two forms: i.e., when conditioning is on the arrival of time, like his saying 'when the month begins you are divorced,' or on the action of a stranger like 'if so-and-so enters the house' or 'if so-and-so prays Zuhr,' she inherits if both condition and conditioning are in illness; due to the existence of escape from him, by his conditioning divorce in a state when the heirs' right to his wealth is attached, i.e., mortal illness.
And if conditioning is in health and occurrence of condition in illness, she does not inherit, contrary to Zufar. For him: that which is conditioned on a condition occurs upon its occurrence, and in his view it is like an immediate (divorce), so it is an occurrence in illness, so he is considered an escaper.
And for us: that conditioning is a divorce upon occurrence of the condition is a legal not intentional matter, and one does not become a wrongful escaper except by intent, and since there is no intent, it is not.
And in the third form: meaning when he conditions it on his own action, she inherits absolutely, whether conditioning is in health or illness, and whether the action has an alternative (i.e., he can avoid doing it) or is unavoidable; because he becomes an escaper either by conditioning in illness or by directly performing the condition in illness. If you say: if the action is unavoidable, he is compelled naturally or legally to do it, so his doing it is not oppression, definitively.
I say: If he has no alternative to the occurrence of the condition, he has an alternative to conditioning on that specific action of his.
And if it (conditioning) is in his health, she does not inherit except in what is unavoidable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, may Allah have mercy on them.
b. And if it (conditioning) is in his health, she does not inherit except in what is unavoidable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar: for she does not inherit according to them; because no action from the husband occurred after her right was attached to his wealth. This is the expression of al-Hidayah, and its meaning: indeed, the wife of the escaper only inherits if there occurred from the husband in his mortal illness an action in invalidating her right after her right was attached to his wealth due to illness, and that action did not occur because conditioning was in his health, rather the wife invalidated her right by performing that action. And in the fourth form: which is when he conditions it on her action: then if both conditioning and condition are in illness, she does not inherit if the action has an alternative for her; because she could have avoided doing it, so when she did it, it is as if she consented to the occurrence of divorce, so the husband is not considered an escaper by it. And she inherits if the action is unavoidable; for then she is compelled to do it, so that is not evidence of her consent. And if conditioning is in his health and condition in illness, she does not inherit if the action has an alternative for her; because she becomes consenting by performing it while able to avoid it. And if the action is unavoidable, she inherits according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; because the husband compelled her (i.e., made her compelled), so the action is attributed to him as if she is his tool, so he becomes an escaper by it. And Zufar and Muhammad said: She does not inherit; because no action from the husband occurred in the state of illness due to conditioning being in health.
[1] His statement: 'and its meaning...' etc.; summary: that the inheritance of the wife of the escaper and invalidation of his divorce in this chapter is only when there occurred from the husband an action that becomes the cause of its occurrence entailing the invalidation of her right in the state of attachment of her right to his wealth (i.e., mortal illness). And in this form, no such action occurred from him because his conditioning was in health, so the occurrence of divorce is attributed to her doing that conditioned action. (2) His statement: 'after it was attached': because the heirs' right attaches to the wealth of the deceased during his mortal illness; hence the prohibition of bequest and gift exceeding one-third in that state except with permission of heirs.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains the intricate rules of inheritance for a wife divorced conditionally during the husband's terminal illness. The key concept is 'firar' (escape): if the husband intends to deprive the wife of inheritance by divorcing her, the divorce is invalidated and she inherits. The passage categorizes conditional divorces based on (a) the type of condition (celestial, third party, husband's act, wife's act) and (b) timing of conditioning and condition occurrence (both in health, conditioning in health & condition in illness, both in illness). For each scenario, it states whether the wife inherits, with disagreements among Hanafi jurists.

- For conditions on celestial events or third parties: if both conditioning and condition occur in illness, she inherits; if conditioning in health and condition in illness, she does not inherit, contrary to Zufar who considers the condition as immediate and thus an escape. The Hanafi response is that escape requires intent, not a legal fiction.
- For conditions on the husband's own act: she inherits absolutely, regardless of timing, because the husband is either escaping by conditioning in illness or by performing the act in illness. The commentary addresses an objection that if the act is unavoidable, he is not oppressive; the answer is that he could have chosen not to condition on that specific act.
- For conditions on the wife's act: there are subcases. If both in illness and the wife has an alternative, she does not inherit because her action implies consent. If no alternative, she inherits (she is compelled). If conditioning in health and condition in illness: if she has an alternative, she does not inherit (as above); if no alternative, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say she inherits because the husband compelled her (he is the escaper), while Muhammad and Zufar say she does not inherit because the husband did no act in illness. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in such cases, as indicated in al-Hidayah and this commentary.

The passage also clarifies the underlying principle: the heirs' right to the estate attaches at the onset of terminal illness, so any act intended to deprive the wife of her share is invalidated.

Key Terms
فرار (firār): The husband's attempt to deprive his wife of inheritance by divorcing her during terminal illness. Such a divorce is invalid, and she inherits.
تعليق (ta‘līq): Conditional pronouncement of divorce, e.g., 'if you do X, you are divorced.' The divorce only occurs when the condition is fulfilled.
بدل (badal): Alternative or option to avoid the condition. If an action has a badal, the person can choose not to do it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a husband's conditional divorce on a celestial event (e.g., 'if the sun rises') result in the wife inheriting?
A) When the conditioning is in health and the condition occurs in illness.
B) When both the conditioning and the condition occur in health.
C) When both the conditioning and the condition occur during the husband's terminal illness.
D) Never, because celestial events are not valid conditions for divorce.

Key Takeaway
For conditional divorces during terminal illness, the wife inherits only when the husband's actions during illness show intent to escape, determined by the condition type and timing.

Wife's Unavoidable Act: The Hanafi Dispute on Firar
Detailed rule for wife's unavoidable act scenario.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a husband conditions divorce on his wife's unavoidable act during his terminal illness, she inherits according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and explain the opposing view of Muhammad and Zufar.

Core Idea
If a wife is compelled to perform the conditioned act, the husband becomes an escaper even if he conditioned in health.

This lesson examines the specific scenario where a husband in good health says to his wife, 'If you do X, you are divorced,' and X is something she cannot avoid (la budda minha). The condition occurs during his terminal illness. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that she inherits because the husband effectively forced her, making him an escaper. Muhammad and Zufar disagree, arguing that no act of the husband occurred during illness. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi jurists weigh intent versus causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the key features: conditioning on the wife's act, conditioning in health, condition (her act) occurs in the husband's terminal illness, and the act is unavoidable (la budda minha).
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: she inherits. Muhammad and Zufar: she does not inherit.
3
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
The husband compelled her (aljā’aha) by conditioning on an unavoidable act, so the act is attributed to him, making him the escaper. The wife is like his tool.
This is based on the principle of ta'liq on unavoidable acts.
4
Analyze the proof of Muhammad and Zufar
No action from the husband occurred after her right attached to his wealth; conditioning was in health, so the wife invalidated her own right by performing the act.
They require a direct act of the husband during illness.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as per al-Hidayah. The wife inherits in this scenario.
This is an example of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

المرض، فيعد فاراً.
ولنا : إنّ كون التعليق تطليقاً عند وجود الشرط أمر حكمي لا قصدي، ولا يصير ظالماً فاراً إلا بالقصد، وإذ ليس فليس.
وفي الوجه الثالث : يعني ما إذا علّقه بفعل نفسه ترث مطلقاً، سواء كان التعليق في الصحة أو في المرض، وسواء كان الفعل تما له بُدَّ منه ؛ أي يمكن منه أن لا يرتكبه، أو كان مما لا بد منه ؛ لأنه يصير فاراً إما بالتعليق في المرض، وإما بمباشرة الشرط في المرض. فإن قلت : إذا كان الفعلُ مما لا بد منه يكون مضطراً طبعاً أو شرعاً إلى إتيانه فلا يكون إتيانه ظلماً قطعاً.
قلت : إن لم يكن له من وجود الشرط بد، فله من التعليق بفعل نفسه الكذائي به
وإن كان في صحته لا ترث إلا فيما لا بُدَّ لها منه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، خلافاً لمحمد وزُفَر الله
ب. وإن كان : أي التعليق في صحته لا ترثُ إلا فيما لا بُدَّ لها منه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، خلافاً لمحمد وزُفَر ) : فإنَّها لا ترث عندهما ؛ لأنه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع بعدما تعلق حقها بماله، هذا عبارةً ((الهداية)) () ، ومعناها : إنَّ امرأة الفار إِنَّما ترثُ إِن وُجِدَ من الزوج في مرض موته صنع في إبطال حقها بعدما تعلق حقها بماله بسبب المرض، ولم يوجد ذلك الصنع ؛ لأنَّ التَّعليق كان في صحته، بل المرأة أبطلت حقها بإتيانها بذلك الفعل. وفي الوجه الرابع : وهو ما إذا علّقه بفعلها، فإن كان التعليق والشرط كلاهما في المرض لا ترث إن كان الفعل مما لها منه بد ؛ لأنه كان يمكن منها أن لا تأتي بالفعل، فلما أتت به كأنها رضيت بوقوع الطلاق، فلا يعد الزوج به فاراً، وترث إن كان الفعل مما لا بد منه، فإنّها حينئذ مضطرة إلى إتيانها ، فلا يكون ذلك دليلاً على رضاها. وإن كان التعليق في صحته والشرط في المرض لا ترث إن كان الفعل مما لها منه تما بد ؛ لأنها تصير راضية بوقوع الطلاق بإتيانه مع إمكان الاحتراز عنه، وإن كان الفعل لا بد منه ترث عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ا ؛ لأن الزوج ألجأها ؛ أي جعلها مضطرة، فينسب الفعل إليه ؛ كأنه آلة له ، فيصير فاراً به. وقال زفر ومحمد : لا ترث؛ لأنه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع في حالة المرض ؛ لكون التعليق في الصحة.
[١]قوله : ومعناها ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن إرث زوجة الفار وإبطال تطليقه في هذا الباب إنّما هو إذا وجد من الزوج فعل يصير باعثاً لوقوعه المتضمن لإبطال حقها في حالة تعلق حقها بماله ، حالة . وهو رض الموت، وفي هذه الصورة لم يوجد منه صنع كذائي ؛ لأنَّ تعليقه كان في الصحة، فينسبُ وقوع الطلاق إلى ارتكابها ذلك الفعل المعلق به. (٢) قوله : بعدما تعلّق ؛ فإنَّ الورثة يتعلّق حقهم بمال الموروث حال مرض موته ، ولهذا نهى عن الوصية والتبرع بما زاد على الثلاث في تلك الحالة إلا بإجازة الورثة.
And if he conditions it on her action: then if both are in his illness, and the action has an alternative for her, she does not inherit; and if it has no alternative for her, she inherits.
3. If conditioned on her action:
a. Then if both (i.e., conditioning and condition) are in his illness, and the action has an alternative for her, she does not inherit; and if it has no alternative for her, she inherits.
[1] His statement: 'then if both...' etc.; clarification of these discussions according to what is in al-Hidayah and its commentaries: Indeed, divorce is either that the husband conditions it on a celestial occurrence like the arrival of a time, or on the action of someone other than them, or on his own action, or on her action. Each aspect is either that the conditioning is in health and the condition in illness, or both in illness; these are eight forms. As for if both conditioning and condition are in health, or conditioning in illness and condition in health, such that he recovered from that illness, it is known from what passed that it is not from the forms of escape (firar). So in the first two forms: i.e., when conditioning is on the arrival of time, like his saying 'when the month begins you are divorced,' or on the action of a stranger like 'if so-and-so enters the house' or 'if so-and-so prays Zuhr,' she inherits if both condition and conditioning are in illness; due to the existence of escape from him, by his conditioning divorce in a state when the heirs' right to his wealth is attached, i.e., mortal illness.
And if conditioning is in health and occurrence of condition in illness, she does not inherit, contrary to Zufar. For him: that which is conditioned on a condition occurs upon its occurrence, and in his view it is like an immediate (divorce), so it is an occurrence in illness, so he is considered an escaper.
And for us: that conditioning is a divorce upon occurrence of the condition is a legal not intentional matter, and one does not become a wrongful escaper except by intent, and since there is no intent, it is not.
And in the third form: meaning when he conditions it on his own action, she inherits absolutely, whether conditioning is in health or illness, and whether the action has an alternative (i.e., he can avoid doing it) or is unavoidable; because he becomes an escaper either by conditioning in illness or by directly performing the condition in illness. If you say: if the action is unavoidable, he is compelled naturally or legally to do it, so his doing it is not oppression, definitively.
I say: If he has no alternative to the occurrence of the condition, he has an alternative to conditioning on that specific action of his.
And if it (conditioning) is in his health, she does not inherit except in what is unavoidable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, may Allah have mercy on them.
b. And if it (conditioning) is in his health, she does not inherit except in what is unavoidable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar: for she does not inherit according to them; because no action from the husband occurred after her right was attached to his wealth. This is the expression of al-Hidayah, and its meaning: indeed, the wife of the escaper only inherits if there occurred from the husband in his mortal illness an action in invalidating her right after her right was attached to his wealth due to illness, and that action did not occur because conditioning was in his health, rather the wife invalidated her right by performing that action. And in the fourth form: which is when he conditions it on her action: then if both conditioning and condition are in illness, she does not inherit if the action has an alternative for her; because she could have avoided doing it, so when she did it, it is as if she consented to the occurrence of divorce, so the husband is not considered an escaper by it. And she inherits if the action is unavoidable; for then she is compelled to do it, so that is not evidence of her consent. And if conditioning is in his health and condition in illness, she does not inherit if the action has an alternative for her; because she becomes consenting by performing it while able to avoid it. And if the action is unavoidable, she inherits according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; because the husband compelled her (i.e., made her compelled), so the action is attributed to him as if she is his tool, so he becomes an escaper by it. And Zufar and Muhammad said: She does not inherit; because no action from the husband occurred in the state of illness due to conditioning being in health.
[1] His statement: 'and its meaning...' etc.; summary: that the inheritance of the wife of the escaper and invalidation of his divorce in this chapter is only when there occurred from the husband an action that becomes the cause of its occurrence entailing the invalidation of her right in the state of attachment of her right to his wealth (i.e., mortal illness). And in this form, no such action occurred from him because his conditioning was in health, so the occurrence of divorce is attributed to her doing that conditioned action. (2) His statement: 'after it was attached': because the heirs' right attaches to the wealth of the deceased during his mortal illness; hence the prohibition of bequest and gift exceeding one-third in that state except with permission of heirs.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains the intricate rules of inheritance for a wife divorced conditionally during the husband's terminal illness. The key concept is 'firar' (escape): if the husband intends to deprive the wife of inheritance by divorcing her, the divorce is invalidated and she inherits. The passage categorizes conditional divorces based on (a) the type of condition (celestial, third party, husband's act, wife's act) and (b) timing of conditioning and condition occurrence (both in health, conditioning in health & condition in illness, both in illness). For each scenario, it states whether the wife inherits, with disagreements among Hanafi jurists.

- For conditions on celestial events or third parties: if both conditioning and condition occur in illness, she inherits; if conditioning in health and condition in illness, she does not inherit, contrary to Zufar who considers the condition as immediate and thus an escape. The Hanafi response is that escape requires intent, not a legal fiction.
- For conditions on the husband's own act: she inherits absolutely, regardless of timing, because the husband is either escaping by conditioning in illness or by performing the act in illness. The commentary addresses an objection that if the act is unavoidable, he is not oppressive; the answer is that he could have chosen not to condition on that specific act.
- For conditions on the wife's act: there are subcases. If both in illness and the wife has an alternative, she does not inherit because her action implies consent. If no alternative, she inherits (she is compelled). If conditioning in health and condition in illness: if she has an alternative, she does not inherit (as above); if no alternative, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say she inherits because the husband compelled her (he is the escaper), while Muhammad and Zufar say she does not inherit because the husband did no act in illness. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in such cases, as indicated in al-Hidayah and this commentary.

The passage also clarifies the underlying principle: the heirs' right to the estate attaches at the onset of terminal illness, so any act intended to deprive the wife of her share is invalidated.

Key Terms
فرار (firār): The husband's attempt to deprive his wife of inheritance by divorcing her during terminal illness. Such a divorce is invalid, and she inherits.
تعليق (ta‘līq): Conditional pronouncement of divorce, e.g., 'if you do X, you are divorced.' The divorce only occurs when the condition is fulfilled.
بدل (badal): Alternative or option to avoid the condition. If an action has a badal, the person can choose not to do it.
لا بد منه (lā budda minhu): Unavoidable; the person cannot reasonably avoid performing the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Any act, regardless of avoidability.
B) Avoidable.
C) Unavoidable.
D) Permissible.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a husband conditions divorce on his wife's unavoidable act during his terminal illness, she inherits because the husband is considered the escaper, even if he conditioned in health.

Inheritance of Wife Divorced by Farr: Condition in Health, Act Unavoidable
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inheritance of wife divorced by farr with condition in health and unavoidable act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling regarding the inheritance of a wife divorced by a farr when the condition was set in health and the act is unavoidable, and articulate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf and Muhammad & Zufar.

Core Idea
A husband who compels his wife to trigger divorce during his illness is a farr, and she inherits despite the condition being set in health.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intricate intra-Hanafi dispute on the inheritance of a wife divorced by a terminally ill husband (farr) who conditioned the divorce on an unavoidable act of the wife. The core disagreement between the founding imams revolves around attributing the divorce: is the husband considered to have fraudulently acted by compelling her, or is the wife’s voluntary (though unavoidable) act the sole cause? Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi methodology of istihsan and its application in protecting the wife’s inheritance rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key facts
Note that the condition (ta'liq) was set in health, the act (shart) occurred during the husband's terminal illness, and the wife was compelled to perform the act (it was unavoidable).
The act must be one she cannot avoid; otherwise, the ruling differs.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
They rule that the wife inherits because the husband's compulsion (ikrah) makes the act attributable to him, rendering him a farr.
The key is that the wife had no choice, so her action does not indicate consent.
3
State the opposing view (Muhammad & Zufar)
They rule that the wife does not inherit because the husband performed no action during illness; the condition was set in health, so the divorce is attributed to the wife's act.
They focus on the absence of any active step by the husband in the death illness.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each position
Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf use istihsan (juristic preference) to analogize to coercion: the husband indirectly caused the divorce. Muhammad & Zufar adhere to the literal requirement that the husband must directly act during illness.
This illustrates how usul principles like qiyas and istihsan operate in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference is whether the wife receives her inheritance share from the husband's estate. According to the relied-upon view (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf), she does.
This protects the wife from being deprived by the husband's fraudulent intent.

كتاب الطلاق طلاق المريض
وإن كان في صحته لا ترث إلا فيما لا بُدَّ لها منه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، خلافاً لمحمد وزفر . وإن كان : أي التعليق في صحته لا ترثُ إلا فيما لا بُدَّ لها منه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، خلافاً لمحمد وزفر ) : فإنَّها لا ترث عندهما ؛ لأنه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع بعدما تعلق حقها بماله، هذا عبارةً ((الهداية)) () ، ومعناها : إنَّ امرأة الفار إِنَّما ترثُ إِن وُجِدَ من الزوج في مرض موته صنع في إبطال حقها بعدما تعلق حقها بماله بسبب المرض، ولم يوجد ذلك الصنع ؛ لأنَّ التَّعليق كان في صحته، بل المرأة أبطلت حقها بإتيانها بذلك الفعل. وفي الوجه الرابع : وهو ما إذا علّقه بفعلها، فإن كان التعليق والشرط كلاهما في المرض لا ترث إن كان الفعل مما لها منه بد ؛ لأنه كان يمكن منها أن لا تأتي بالفعل، فلما أتت به كأنها رضيت بوقوع الطلاق، فلا يعد الزوج به فاراً، وترث إن كان الفعل مما لا بد منه، فإنّها حينئذ مضطرة إلى إتيانها ، فلا يكون ذلك دليلاً على رضاها. وإن كان التعليق في صحته والشرط في المرض لا ترث إن كان الفعل مما لها منه بد ؛ لأنها تصير راضية بوقوع الطلاق بإتيانه مع إمكان الاحتراز عنه، وإن كان الفعل لا بد منه ترث عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ا ؛ لأن الزوج ألجأها ؛ أي جعلها مضطرة، فينسب الفعل إليه ؛ كأنه آلة له ، فيصير فاراً به. وقال زفر ومحمد : لا ترث؛ لأنه لم يوجد من الزوج صنع في حالة المرض ؛ لكون التعليق في الصحة.
[١]قوله : ومعناها ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن إرث زوجة الفار وإبطال تطليقه في هذا الباب إنّما هو إذا وجد من الزوج فعل يصير باعثاً لوقوعه المتضمن لإبطال حقها في حالة تعلق حقها بماله، حالة . وهو رض الموت، وفي هذه الصورة لم يوجد منه صنع كذائي ؛ لأنَّ تعليقه كان في الصحة، فينسبُ وقوع الطلاق إلى ارتكابها ذلك الفعل المعلق به. (٢) قوله : بعدما تعلّق ؛ فإنَّ الورثة يتعلّق حقهم بمال الموروث حال مرض موته ، ولهذا نهى عن الوصية والتبرع بما زاد على الثلاث في تلك الحالة إلا بإجازة الورثة.
(1) ((الهداية» (٢ : ٥).
Book of Divorce: Divorce of the Sick. And if it [the condition] was in his health, she does not inherit except for what is unavoidable for her according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar. And if it was: i.e., the condition in his health, she does not inherit except for what is unavoidable for her according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar: for she does not inherit according to them because there was no action from the husband after her right became attached to his property. This is the expression of al-Hidayah, and its meaning is that the wife of the farr only inherits if an action from the husband in his terminal illness to invalidate her right occurred after her right became attached to his property due to illness, and that action did not occur because the condition was in his health; rather, the woman invalidated her right by performing that act. And in the fourth scenario: which is when he conditioned it upon her act, if both the condition and the occurrence are in illness, she does not inherit if the act is avoidable for her, because she could have not performed the act, so when she performed it, it is as if she consented to the divorce, so the husband is not considered a farr by it; and she inherits if the act is unavoidable, for then she is compelled to perform it, so that is not evidence of her consent. And if the condition was in his health and the occurrence in illness, she does not inherit if the act is avoidable for her, because she becomes consenting to the divorce by performing it while able to avoid it; and if the act is unavoidable, she inherits according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the husband compelled her, i.e., made her compelled, so the act is attributed to him as if he is an instrument for it, so he becomes a farr by it. And Zufar and Muhammad said: she does not inherit because there was no action from the husband in the state of illness, since the condition was in health. [1] His saying: 'and its meaning... etc.'; its summary is that the inheritance of the farr's wife and the nullification of his divorce in this chapter is only when an action from the husband occurs that becomes a cause for its occurrence, which entails the nullification of her right at a time when her right is attached to his property, i.e., the death illness, and in this scenario no such action occurred from him because his condition was in health, so the occurrence of the divorce is attributed to her committing that act upon which it was conditioned. (2) His saying: 'after it became attached'; because the heirs' right becomes attached to the deceased's property during his death illness, and for this reason, bequest and donation beyond one-third in that state are prohibited except with the heirs' permission. (1) Al-Hidayah (2:5).
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the inheritance rights of a wife divorced by a terminally ill husband (farr). The core issue is whether the husband is considered to have fraudulently deprived his wife of inheritance when the divorce is conditional upon an act of the wife. The passage, based on al-Hidayah, presents four scenarios: (1) condition and act both in health (the wife does not inherit, as no fraudulent action by husband), (2) condition and act both in illness (if act is avoidable, no inheritance; if unavoidable, wife inherits because she is compelled), (3) condition in health, act in illness with avoidable act (no inheritance, as she consented), (4) condition in health, act in illness with unavoidable act (dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule inheritance because the husband compelled her, attributing the act to him; Muhammad and Zufar deny inheritance because no husband action during illness). The dispute hinges on whether the husband's conditional pronouncement in health constitutes a 'fraudulent act' when the wife is compelled to perform an unavoidable act. The commentary emphasizes the principle that the farr's wife inherits only if the husband actively invalidates her right after her right attached to his property due to illness—here, the act is attributed to him via compulsion, making him a farr. The passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of istihsan (juristic preference) and analogy to coercion (ikrah) in attributing acts.

Key Terms
الفار (al-fār): A husband who divorces his wife in his terminal illness with the intent to deprive her of inheritance.
التعليق (al-ta‘līq): The husband's conditional statement that the divorce will occur upon the happening of a future act.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): The event or act upon which the divorce is conditioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the farr conditions divorce in health and the unavoidable act occurs in illness, what do Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule?
A) The wife does not inherit because the act is attributed to her.
B) The wife inherits because the husband is considered to have compelled her.
C) The wife inherits only if the divorce was revocable.
D) The wife does not inherit because no action from the husband in illness.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a husband conditionally divorces his wife during health on an unavoidable act that occurs during his terminal illness, he is considered a farr by compulsion, and the wife inherits according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the relied-upon position.

Inheritance of the Wife in Revocable Divorce
Ruling with proof and cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance of a wife in revocable divorce and explain the proof based on the partial survival of marriage during iddah.

Core Idea
A wife in revocable divorce inherits during her iddah because marriage partially remains.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that a wife who is in a revocable divorce (talāq raj‘ī) inherits from her husband if he dies during her ‘iddah. The ruling is based on the principle that revocable divorce does not completely sever the marriage bond; several marital effects persist, making inheritance possible. We will explore the proof, the consensus after iddah expiry, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi‘i.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the exact ruling: a wife in revocable divorce inherits from her husband if he dies during her ‘iddah, in all circumstances. Note that this applies regardless of how the divorce occurred.
The text says 'in all cases' (fī al-aḥwāl ajma‘).
2
Identify the consensus point
Recognize that all scholars agree: if the ‘iddah expires and then the husband dies, the wife does not inherit. This is an agreed exception.
Consensus (ijmā‘) between Hanafis and Shafi‘is.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on qiyās: revocable divorce does not remove marriage completely. Evidence: intercourse remains permissible during ‘iddah, and the husband has the right to take her back (raj‘ah). Also, marrying certain relatives is prohibited during ‘iddah. Thus, the cause of inheritance (marriage) partially persists.
The dalīl is aqli (rational analogy).
4
Consider the Shafi‘i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi‘i argued that divorce severs the marriage entirely, so inheritance does not apply. The Hanafi response is that marriage survives in some respects during ‘iddah, as evidenced by the prohibitions mentioned. Therefore, inheritance is valid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf on the nature of revocable divorce.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Take a concrete case: A man divorces his wife with a revocable divorce. He dies on the 10th day of her 90-day ‘iddah. She inherits. If he dies after day 90, she does not.
The key is timing of death relative to ‘iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الرجعي ترث في الأحوال أجمع
وخُص إرثها بموته في عدّتِها : أما إذا انقضت عدتُها، ثم مات لا ترث إجماعاً
[١] قوله : فجوابهما ؛ أي الجواب من قبل أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، وحاصله : أن تعليقه وإن كان في الصحة لكن لَمَّا علقه بفعل لا بد لها منه ، فهي مضطرة إلى إتيانها في كلّ . حالة ، فكأنه وقع الصنع في إبطال حقها منه.
[٢] قوله : كما في الإكراه ؛ فإنّه إذا أكره زيد عمراً على إتلاف مال الغير، فأتلفه عمرو يجب ضمانه على زيد ؛ لأنَّ المكره بالفتح صـار كـأنـه آلـة للمـكـره بالكسر ، كالسكين للذابح ، فانتقل الفعل إليه.
ويصير
[٣]قوله : في الأحوال أجمع ؛ يعني سواءً كان الطلاق بسؤالها أو بغير سؤالها ، وسواء كان التعليق بفعلها أو بفعله، وسواء كان الفعل ما له منه بد، ولا وذلك ؛ لأنَّ الطلاق الرجعي لا يزيل النكاح من كل وجه، حتى يحـل الـوطء في الـعـدة ، رجعة ، فكان سبب الإرث قائما. كذا في «العناية»(۳). (٤) قوله : لا ترث إجماعاً ؛ أي بيننا وبين الشافعي له وغيره، وذلك لانقطاع الزوجية مطلقاً عند موته، وهي من أسباب الإرث ، ويشترط في الإرث وجود سبب من أسباب الإرث عند موت المورث ، وبهذا احتج الشافعي له فيما قبل انقضاء العدة أيضاً.
والفرق لنا : أنَّ العدّة يبقى فيها النكاح في بعض الأحكام ؛ ولهذا لا يحل له نكاح الأخت في عدّة الأخت ونكاحُ الخامسة في عدة الرابعة، فيجوز أن يحكم ببقاء النكاح
And in the revocable [divorce], she inherits in all cases. And her inheritance is restricted to his death during her 'iddah: as for when her 'iddah expires, then he dies, she does not inherit by consensus. [1] His saying: 'So their answer'; i.e., the answer from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and its summary is that his condition, even if in health, since he conditioned it upon an act unavoidable for her, she is compelled to perform it in any case, so it is as if the action of invalidating her right occurred from him. [2] His saying: 'as in coercion'; for if Zayd coerced 'Amr to destroy property of another, and 'Amr destroyed it, the liability falls on Zayd because the coerced person becomes like an instrument of the coercer, like the knife for the slaughterer, so the act transfers to him. [3] His saying: 'in all cases'; meaning whether the divorce was at her request or not, whether the condition was by her act or his, and whether the act was avoidable or not, because the revocable divorce does not remove the marriage completely, to the extent that intercourse is permissible during the 'iddah, and he has the right to take her back, so the cause of inheritance remains. As in al-‘Inayah. (4) His saying: 'she does not inherit by consensus'; i.e., between us and al-Shafi‘i, because the marital tie is absolutely severed at his death, and that is one of the causes of inheritance, and it is a condition for inheritance that a cause of inheritance exist at the time of the inheritor's death. And with this al-Shafi‘i argued also for the period before the expiry of the 'iddah. And our distinction is that during the 'iddah, marriage remains in some rulings; for this reason, it is not permissible for him to marry the sister during the sister's 'iddah and the fifth wife during the fourth wife's 'iddah, so it is permissible to rule that the marriage remains.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the inheritance of a wife who is in a revocable divorce (talāq raj‘ī). The text states unequivocally that such a wife inherits from her husband if he dies during her ‘iddah (waiting period), in all circumstances regardless of how the divorce occurred. However, if the ‘iddah has expired and she dies, she does not inherit by consensus. The commentary explains that this ruling is based on the principle that a revocable divorce does not completely sever the marriage bond; several marital effects remain, such as the permissibility of intercourse during the ‘iddah and the husband's right to take her back without a new marriage contract. Thus, the cause of inheritance (the marriage) is still partially present. The passage then addresses an objection from Imam al-Shafi‘i, who argued that since divorce severs the marriage, the wife should not inherit even during the ‘iddah. The Hanafi response is that the ‘iddah preserves some aspects of marriage, as evidenced by the prohibition of marrying the wife's sister or a fifth wife during the ‘iddah. Therefore, inheritance remains. This ruling underscores the Hanafi position that the incomplete nature of revocable divorce keeps the wife as an inheritor.

Key Terms
الرجعي (al-raj‘ī): A revocable divorce where the husband can take his wife back during her ‘iddah without a new contract.
العدة (al-‘iddah): The waiting period after divorce during which the wife cannot remarry and certain marital effects persist.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does a wife in a revocable divorce (raj‘ī) inherit from her deceased husband?
A) She inherits only if the divorce was at her request.
B) She inherits if he dies during her ‘iddah, regardless of how the divorce occurred.
C) She inherits only if the divorce was initiated by the husband.
D) She inherits only if the iddah has already expired.

Key Takeaway
In revocable divorce, the wife inherits if the husband dies during her ‘iddah because the marriage is not fully dissolved.
